   A.   Fee: Each licensee to whom a license is issued under the provision of
this article shall pay to the City in advance, an annual license fee of two
hundred twenty five dollars ($225.00). (1990 Code §5-410)
   B.   Term: All licenses issued hereunder shall expire at twelve o'clock (12:
00) midnight on January 31st of the calendar year for which issued. The license
fee shall be for the entire year and shall not be prorated but shall be paid in
full at the beginning of each year. (1990 Code §5-410; amd. 2018 Code)
   C.   Refund: No refund shall be allowed for any canceled, revoked or unused
license. No rebate or discount of annual license fee shall be granted or
allowed for any year. (1990 Code §5-410)
2-2A-9: PREMISES AND LOCATION REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Sanitation: All licensed premises shall be maintained in sanitary
condition according to the requirements of Idaho Department of Health and
Welfare licensing requirements, as amended. (1990 Code §5-412; amd. 2018 Code)
   B.   Location Restrictions; Exceptions: No license shall be issued for any
premises in any neighborhood which is predominantly residential or within two
hundred feet (200') of any public school, church or any other place of worship,
measured in a straight line to the nearest entrance to the licensed premises;
provided, that this limitation shall not apply to any duly licensed premises
that at the time of licensing did not come within the restricted area, but
subsequent to the licensing came therein. (1990 Code §5-413)
   C.   Examination Of Premises: Any officer of the City, Sheriff, Constable or
police officer of the State of Idaho shall have the right at any time to make
an examination of the premises of any licensee to ascertain whether the laws of
the State of Idaho, the County of Lewis or the United States of America and
this Code are being complied with, and it shall be unlawful to refuse such
officer the right to admittance or access to such premises. It is hereby made
the duty of such officers knowing of any violation of this article, to make
complaints before the proper officers and to assist in the prosecution and
conviction of offenders. (1990 Code §5-420)
2-2A-10: HOURS OF SALE:
It shall be unlawful to sell liquor or offer liquor for sale or otherwise
dispose of the same, or permit liquor to be consumed upon any premises operated
under licenses issued in accordance with the provisions of this article,
between the hours of two o'clock (2:00) A.M. and ten o'clock (10:00) A.M. on
any day. (2018 Code)
2-2A-11: GAMBLING PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any licensee to permit, conduct, play, carry on, open
or cause to be opened any gaming in or upon licensed premises or in or upon any
premises directly connected by a door, hallway or other means of access from
the licensed premises, except such forms of gaming as are authorized by the
laws of the State of Idaho and the City. (1990 Code §5-415)
2-2A-12: RESTRICTION OF SALES BY LICENSEE:
No licensee or his or its employees, agents, servants or bartenders shall sell,
deliver or give away, or cause or permit to be sold, delivered, or given away
any liquor to:
   A.   Any person under the age of twenty one (21) years.
   B.   Any person actually, apparently or obviously intoxicated.
   C.   An interdicted person. (1990 Code §5-416)
2-2A-13: PURCHASE BY UNQUALIFIED PERSON:
Any person under the age of twenty one (21) years or other person who knowingly
misrepresents his or her qualifications for the purpose of obtaining liquor
from such licensee shall be equally guilty with such licensee and shall, upon
conviction thereof, be guilty of a misdemeanor. (1990 Code §5-417)
2-2A-14: INTOXICATED PERSONS:
No intoxicated person shall be permitted to remain in, loiter or loaf in the
place of business of any licensee and the licensee and his agents, servants or
bartenders shall give any and all necessary and required assistance to any
police of the County or State in evicting and removing said person from the
premises. (1990 Code §5-418)
2-2A-15: RESTRICTIONS ON SALES AND ADVERTISING:
   A.   Liquor In Original Containers: It shall be unlawful for any licensee to
sell, keep for sale, dispense, give away or otherwise dispose of any liquor in
the original containers or otherwise than by retail sale by the drink for
consumption only upon the licensed premises.
   B.   Liquor Purchased From State Liquor Dispensary: No liquor shall be sold
by any licensee, except the same which has been purchased by the licensee from
the Idaho Liquor Dispensary through its regular retail stores and distributors.
   C.   Advertising: It shall be unlawful for any licensee to adopt or use any
name, sign or advertisement outside of the licensed premises advertising the
handling or sale of liquor therein. (1990 Code §5-419)
2-2A-16: UNLICENSED ROOMS UNLAWFUL:
It shall be unlawful for any person to keep or maintain any room or premises in
which liquor is received or kept, whether owned by such person or by another,
or to which liquor is brought, for consumption on the premises by members of
the public or of any club incorporated or unincorporated or a corporation or
association, unless such person and the premises are licensed under this
article. (1990 Code §5-421)
2-2A-17: LICENSE REVOCATION OR CANCELLATION; HEARING:
The right shall be, and at all times shall remain, vested in the City Council
to revoke or cancel the license of any person licensed hereunder for any
violation of this article, and upon verified complaint filed with the Council,
the Council shall, by written notice, cause such alleged offender to appear
before said Council and be heard upon said complaint. A copy of such complaint
shall be served with such notice, and the day and hour of the hearing, which
shall be at least five (5) days hence, shall be specified in such notice, and
such hearing shall be had in City Hall unless a different place shall be
specified in such notice. If at said hearing upon the taking of evidence on
behalf of the City and such alleged offender, it shall appear to said Council
that cause exists for the cancellation or revocation of such license, the same
may be canceled or revoked without further process of law. Upon such
cancellation or revocation, no refund of any unexpired portion of the license
fee shall be made to the licensee; and the fact of such revocation shall
immediately be certified to the Director of Idaho State Police by the City
Clerk-Treasurer, and, if any conviction is had hereunder in the Police Court
for Lewis County, a certified copy of the judgment therein shall be immediately
certified to said Director. (1990 Code §5-422; amd. 2018 Code)
2-2A-18: PENALTY:
Any person violating the provisions of this article shall, upon conviction
thereof, be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished pursuant to
section
1-4-1 of this Code. (1990 Code §5-424)
ARTICLE B. BEER
SECTION:
2-2B-1: Definitions
2-2B-2: Alcoholic Content
2-2B-3: Licensing Requirements
2-2B-4: Application For License; Conditions And Requirements
2-2B-5: Qualifications Of Licensee
2-2B-6: License Fees; Term Of License
2-2B-7: Transfer Of License; Fee
2-2B-8: Power To Refuse, Revoke And Inspect
2-2B-9: Serving Underage Person
2-2B-10: Drinking Beer In Unlicensed Public Places
2-2B-11: Beer Sales At Dances Or Dance Halls; Permit
2-2B-12: Hours Of Sale
2-2B-13: Penalty
2-2B-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this article, the following terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
BEER: Any beverage obtained by the alcoholic fermentation of an infusion or
decoction of barley, malt, and/or other ingredients in drinkable water.
RETAILER: Any person engaged in the sale or distribution of beer to the
consumer.
YEAR: A calendar year.
(1990 Code §5-301; amd. 2018 Code)
2-2B-2: ALCOHOLIC CONTENT:
   A.   Beer containing not more than six percent (6%) of alcohol by weight may
be manufactured, imported and/or sold and distributed in and into this City or
possessed therein in the manner and under the conditions prescribed in this
article and not otherwise.
   B.   Beer containing more than four percent (4%) of alcohol by weight shall
be considered and taxed as wine. (1990 Code §5-302; amd. 2018 Code)
2-2B-3: LICENSING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   License Required: It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or
corporation to sell beer, or offer beer for sale at retail to the consumer
without first obtaining a license therefor from the City, and a separate
license shall be required for each place of business where beer is sold. (1990
Code §5-303)
   B.   Separate Licenses: Separate licenses shall be obtained and required for
each place of business operated by any retailer. (1990 Code §5-308)
   C.   Posting Of License: It shall be the duty of each person to whom a
license is issued under this article to keep the same displayed in a
conspicuous place within the premises for which issued. (1990 Code §5-309)
   D.   Fractional Licenses: No fractional or part time licenses shall be
issued. (1990 Code §5-310)
2-2B-4: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE; CONDITIONS AND REQUIREMENTS:
All applications for licenses shall be in writing and filed with the City
Clerk-Treasurer upon forms to be furnished by said Clerk-Treasurer, and such
application must be accompanied by the license fee prescribed therein and shall
meet the following specifications and conditions:
   A.   All applications for beer licenses shall, accompanied by the prescribed
fees, be filed with the City Clerk-Treasurer, who shall note thereon the date
and hour of receipt. The Clerk-Treasurer shall thereupon examine the
application for completeness and proper form. If it is deemed insufficient, it
shall be forthwith returned to the applicant with a written statement of
deficiencies and may be resubmitted at any time thereafter. When deemed to be
in proper form by the Clerk- Treasurer, the consideration of said application
shall be placed upon the agenda for the next meeting of the City Council, but
in no event later than thirty (30) days following the acceptance of said
application by the Clerk-Treasurer. The Council shall render a decision upon
the application at the first meeting that it appears on the agenda unless
consideration is tabled for good cause shown, but in no event later than sixty
(60) days following the acceptance of the application by the Clerk-Treasurer.
   B.   In all cases where the Council is considering the application for a new
beer license or the renewal of an existing beer license, a transcribable
verbatim recording of the proceedings shall be made as well as keeping minutes
of the proceedings. These records shall be retained for no less a period of
time than that which may be prescribed by the laws of the State of Idaho.
   C.   Whenever the City Council shall deny an application hereunder, the
Council shall specify in writing:
      1.   The statutes, ordinances and standards used in evaluating the
application;
      2.   The reasons for denial; and
      3.   The actions, if any, that the applicant would take to obtain the
license or renewal thereof. (1990 Code §5-304)
2-2B-5: QUALIFICATIONS OF LICENSEE:
No retail license shall be issued to an applicant who is not a person of good
moral character and/or repute, and twenty one (21) years of age or older, nor
shall any such license be granted to any applicant who is not a citizen of the
United States, or has not been a bona fide resident of the State of Idaho for a
period of thirty (30) days prior to the date of making application, or who
shall have been convicted for the violation of any law of the State of Idaho or
the United States of America or of this City regulating, governing or
prohibiting the sale of alcoholic beverages, or intoxicating liquor; provided,
however, in case the applicant is a partnership, the requirements relative to
residence shall be deemed satisfied when any member of the partnership or the
actual manager thereof has been a bona fide resident of the State of Idaho for
a period of thirty (30) days prior to the date of making such application, and
if the applicant is a corporation, such corporation shall be qualified to do
business within the State of Idaho, and the manager of such business place
shall be such citizen and shall have been such resident; nor shall any person
be permitted to receive or hold a license under this article for use in
connection with any business not under the personal supervision, management and
control of said person to whom said license is issued. (1990 Code §5-305)
2-2B-6: LICENSE FEES; TERM OF LICENSE:
   A.   Fees: The annual license fees shall be as follows:
      1.   The license fee for any retailer selling beer, any of which is
consumed or to be consumed on the premises where sold, shall be one hundred
twenty five dollars ($125.00) per year or any part thereof.
      2.   The license fee for any retailer selling beer, none of which is
consumed or to be consumed on the premises where sold, is hereby fixed at fifty
dollars ($50.00) per year or any part thereof. (1990 Code §5-306)
   B.   Term: All licenses issued under the provisions of this article shall
expire at twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight on January 31st of the year in which
issued. (1990 Code §5-306; amd. 2018 Code)
   C.   Refunds: No refunds shall be allowed for any canceled, revoked or
unused licensee. (1990 Code §5-311)
2-2B-7: TRANSFER OF LICENSE; FEE:
   A.   No license granted under the terms of this article, when transferred by
process of law or otherwise, shall authorize the transferee, including any
executor, administrator or trustee in bankruptcy of the estate of the licensee,
to retail beer thereunder until the transferee shall have filed application
therefor containing substantially the same information required of an applicant
for a license, and if the transferee possesses the qualifications and none of
the disqualifications for a license as herein provided, the City shall approve
such transfer and amend the license so to show.
   B.   Such transferee shall accompany each such application for transfer
with, and shall pay, the sum of five dollars ($5.00). (1990 Code §5-307)
2-2B-8: POWER TO REFUSE, REVOKE AND INSPECT:
   A.   Council Authority: The City Council shall have the power to refuse a
license to any applicant, and/or revoke a license at any time when in the
judgment of the said Council the business interests and the welfare of the
City, and/or the inhabitants thereof, will be best served by the denial or
revocation thereof; and for the purpose of ascertaining whether or not any
licensee is conforming with this or any other articles or chapters of this
Code, as well as the laws of the State of Idaho, the police shall have the
right, at all reasonable times, to inspect the places where beer is sold under
the licenses issued. Provided further, that any license issued under the
provisions of this article shall be forfeited, canceled and revoked by order of
the City Council, if, after the issuance thereof and during the period for
which said license shall have been issued, the holder thereof shall fail to
possess all the qualifications enumerated as prerequisites to then obtaining of
such license. The City Clerk-Treasurer, upon such revocation, shall, in
writing, send by United States certified mail a notification to the other
issuers of other retailer's license to such licensee, stating sufficient facts
for identification of the licensee, and the grounds and date of such
revocation.
   B.   Investigation: No license shall be issued by the City Clerk-Treasurer
until each applicant has been properly and adequately investigated by the
County Sheriff, and the prior approval of the City Council has been obtained.
(1990 Code §5-312)
2-2B-9: SERVING UNDERAGE PERSON:
It shall be unlawful to sell or serve beer to any minor under the age of twenty
one (21) years. (1990 Code §5-313)
2-2B-10: DRINKING BEER IN UNLICENSED PUBLIC PLACES:
No person shall drink beer upon any public highway or street or other public
place within the limits of the City unless said place has been licensed by the
City Council as a place where beer may be sold at retail. (1990 Code §5-314)
2-2B-11: BEER SALES AT DANCES OR DANCE HALLS; PERMIT:
It shall be unlawful to sell beer or offer beer for sale or otherwise dispose
of the same at any public dance, or at any public dance hall within the City
unless there shall have been issued a proper catering permit under the State
law for such time, place and event. (1990 Code §5-315)
2-2B-12: HOURS OF SALE:
It shall be unlawful to sell beer or offer beer for sale or otherwise dispose
of the same, or permit beer to be consumed upon any premises operated under
licenses issued in accordance with the provisions of this article, between the
hours of two o'clock (2:00) A.M. and six o'clock (6:00) A.M. on any day. (1990
Code §5-316)
2-2B-13: PENALTY:
Any person violating the provisions of this article shall, upon conviction
thereof, be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished pursuant to
section 1-4-1 of this Code. (1990 Code §5-318)
ARTICLE C. WINE
SECTION:
2-2C-1: Definitions
2-2C-2: Licensing Requirements; Fee
2-2C-3: Sale Of Wine
2-2C-4: License Issuance; Investigation
2-2C-5: Transfer Of License; Fee
2-2C-6: Off-Premises Consumption
2-2C-7: Restrictions On Sales And Advertising
2-2C-8: Drinking Wine In Unlicensed Public Places
2-2C-9: Restrictions Concerning Underage Persons
2-2C-10: Revocation Or Suspension Of License; Hearing
2-2C-11: Violation A Misdemeanor
2-2C-1: DEFINITIONS:
All words and phrases used in this article, the definition of which is not
herein given, shall be given their ordinary and commonly understood and
accepted meanings.
For the purpose of this article, the following terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
PERSON: An individual, firm, copartnership, association, corporation, or any
group or combination acting as a unit, and includes the plural as well as the
singular unless the intent to give a more limited meaning is disclosed by the
context in which it is used.
RETAIL WINE LICENSE: A license issued by the City authorizing a person to sell
wine at retail for off-premises consumption only.
RETAILER: A person to whom a retail wine license has been issued hereunder.
STATE LICENSE; COUNTY LICENSE: "State license" shall mean a retail wine license
issued by the Director of Idaho State Police, and "County license" shall mean a
retail wine license issued by the Board of County Commissioners of Lewis
County, Idaho.
WINE: Any alcoholic beverage containing not more than fourteen percent (14%)
alcohol by volume obtained by the fermentation of the natural sugar content of
fruits or other agricultural products containing sugar.
(1990 Code §5-501; amd. 2018 Code)
2-2C-2: LICENSING REQUIREMENTS; FEE:
   A.   License Required: No person shall sell wine at retail unless he
possesses a valid license therefor, issued pursuant to the provisions of this
article. (1990 Code §5-503)
   B.   Application For License: All applications for a license hereunder shall
be made on forms provided by the City Clerk- Treasurer and shall be accompanied
by the appropriate fee. (1990 Code §5-508)
   C.   State And County Licenses Required: No retail wine license issued by
the City Council shall authorize the retailer to sell wine at retail unless
such person possesses a State and County license. (1990 Code §5-510)
   D.   License Fee: There is hereby established a license fee of one dollar
($1.00). (1990 Code §5-504)
   E.   Separate License For Each Premises: A separate retail wine license
shall be required for each premises; provided, however, nothing herein shall
prohibit a distributor or retailer from possessing licenses for more than one
premises. (1990 Code §5-505)
   F.   Fractional Licenses: No fractional or part year licenses shall be
issued. All licenses issued hereunder shall expire on January 31st at twelve
o'clock (12:00) midnight in the year following the year in which it is issued.
(1990 Code §5-507; amd. 2018 Code)
   G.   Posting Of License: All licenses issued hereunder shall be on forms
provided by the City Clerk-Treasurer and shall be posted by the licensee in a
conspicuous place in his place of business. (1990 Code §5-509)
2-2C-3: SALE OF WINE:
   A.   Retailers holding valid licenses for the retail sale of liquor by the
drink pursuant to article A of this chapter may sell wine for consumption on or
off the licensed premises.
   B.   Retailers who do not possess a valid license for the retail sale of
liquor by the drink shall not permit consumption of wine on the licensed
premises and may sell the wine only in its original unbroken container. (1990
Code §5-514)
   C.   Wine sold for consumption on the retailer's premises may be sold only
during hours that beer can be sold pursuant to the laws of this State. (1990
Code §5-514; amd. 2018 Code)
   D.   Wine sold by a retailer for consumption off the premises of the
retailer may be sold only during the hours that beer may be sold pursuant to
the laws of this State. (1990 Code §5-514)
2-2C-4: LICENSE ISSUANCE; INVESTIGATION:
Upon the receipt of an application for a license under this article,
accompanied by the necessary fee, the City Council may make such investigation
of all matters pertaining thereto as it shall deem proper. If the Council shall
determine that the contents of the application are true, that such applicant is
qualified to receive a license, that the premises are suitable for the carrying
on of the intended business, and that the requirements of this article have
been met and complied with, a license shall be issued; otherwise, the
application shall be denied and the license fee returned. (1990 Code §5-511)
2-2C-5: TRANSFER OF LICENSE; FEE:
   A.   No license granted under the terms of this article, when transferred by
process of law or otherwise, shall authorize the transferee, including any
executor, administrator or trustee in bankruptcy of the estate of the licensee,
to retail wine thereunder until the transferee shall have filed application
therefor containing substantially the same information required of an applicant
for a license, and if the transferee possesses the qualifications and none of
the disqualifications for a license as herein provided, the City shall approve
such transfer and amend the licenses so to show.
   B.   Such transferee shall accompany each such application for transfer
with, and shall pay, the sum of five dollars ($5.00). (1990 Code §5-506)
2-2C-6: OFF-PREMISES CONSUMPTION:
The sale of wine at retail within the corporate limits of the City, for off-
premises consumption only, is hereby authorized, subject to the provisions of
this article. (1990 Code §5-502)
2-2C-7: RESTRICTIONS ON SALES AND ADVERTISING:
Any ordinance to the contrary notwithstanding, including, but not limited to,
subsection 2-2A-15B of this chapter, the holder of a license for the retail
sale of liquor by the drink as defined in article A of this chapter, is hereby
authorized to purchase wine from persons holding valid wine distributors'
licenses or wine retailers' licenses. (1990 Code §5-513)
2-2C-8: DRINKING WINE IN UNLICENSED PUBLIC PLACES:
No person shall drink wine upon any public highway or street or other public
place within the limits of the City unless said place has been licensed by the
City Council as a place where liquor by the drink may be sold at retail for on-
premises consumption. (1990 Code §5-515)
2-2C-9: RESTRICTIONS CONCERNING UNDERAGE PERSONS:
   A.   No person under the age of twenty one (21) years may purchase, consume
or possess wine.
   B.   No person shall give, sell or deliver wine to any person under the age
of twenty one (21) years.
   C.   No person under the age of twenty one (21) years shall by any means
represent to any retailer or to any agent or employee of such retailer that he
or she is twenty one (21) years or more of age for the purpose of inducing such
retailer or his agent or employee to sell, serve or dispense wine to such
person. (1990 Code §5-516)
2-2C-10: REVOCATION OR SUSPENSION OF LICENSE; HEARING:
The right shall be, and at all times shall remain, vested in the City Council
to revoke, cancel or suspend the license of any person licensed hereunder for
any violation of this article or of any violation of any County ordinance,
State or Federal law relating to the sale of wine; and, upon verified complaint
filed with the Council, the Council shall, by written notice, cause such
alleged offender to appear before such Council and be heard upon said
complaint. A copy of such complaint shall be served with such notice, and the
day, hour and place of hearing, which shall be at least five (5) days hence,
shall be specified in such notice. If at such hearing, upon the taking of
evidence on behalf of the City and such alleged offender, it shall appear to
said Council that cause exists for the cancellation or revocation of such
license, the same may be canceled, revoked or suspended without further process
of law, and the fact of such cancellation, revocation or suspension shall
immediately be certified to the Director of Idaho State Police and the Board of
Commissioners of Lewis County. (1990 Code §5-512; amd. 2018 Code)
2-2C-11: VIOLATION A MISDEMEANOR:
Any person who violates any of the provisions of this article or fails to
comply with any of the terms and conditions of this article shall be guilty of
a misdemeanor. (1990 Code §5-517)
TITLE 3
HEALTH, SANITATION AND ENVIRONMENT
CHAPTER 1
NUISANCES
SECTION:
3-1-1: Nuisance Defined
3-1-2: Destruction Of Dilapidated Or Unsafe Buildings
3-1-3: Maintaining Nuisance Prohibited
3-1-4: Liability For Abatement
3-1-5: Abatement By City
3-1-6: Garbage And Refuse On Streets, Sidewalks Or Public Grounds
3-1-7: Trash And Junk On Private Property; Abatement
3-1-1: NUISANCE DEFINED:
Anything which is injurious to the health or morals, or which is indecent or
offensive to the senses or an obstruction to the free use of property so as to
interfere with the comfortable enjoyment of life or property, or which
unlawfully obstructs free passage or use in the customary manner of any street,
alley, sidewalk or public park, or injures any street or alley, or disturbs the
peace and quiet, is hereby declared to be a "nuisance". (1990 Code §6-601)
3-1-2: DESTRUCTION OF DILAPIDATED OR UNSAFE BUILDINGS:
   A.   Prohibited Condition; Council Authority: It shall be unlawful to
maintain any building or property so dilapidated or in such condition as to
menace the public health or safety, and the City Council may cause the
destruction or removal of the same at the expense of the person creating,
causing or maintaining the building or property.
   B.   Special Assessment: The City may impose a special assessment on the
land or premises where such building or property is situated, sufficient to
defray the cost of abating the nuisance thereby created. (1990 Code §6-602)
3-1-3: MAINTAINING NUISANCE PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to create or maintain any nuisance to be
created, maintained or to exist on premises owned by him or under his control.
(1990 Code §6-605)
3-1-4: LIABILITY FOR ABATEMENT:
It shall be the duty of the owner of any property whereon any nuisance exists
or of the lessee, manager or person in charge thereof to remove, abate or
destroy the same without delay. (1990 Code §6-603)
3-1-5: ABATEMENT BY CITY:
Whenever any nuisance exists for the abatement, creation or removal of which no
responsible person can be found, it shall be the duty of the properly
designated City officer to remove, abate or destroy the same or cause the same
to be done. (1990 Code §6-604)
3-1-6: GARBAGE AND REFUSE ON STREETS, SIDEWALKS OR PUBLIC GROUNDS:
   A.   Any person, firm or corporation who shall willfully or negligently
throw, dump, store or deposit upon any sidewalk, street, alley or public place,
or any portion thereof, any glass, nails, tacks, hoops, cane, barbed wire,
boards, or any other substance or material which would be likely to injure any
animal, vehicle or person traveling thereon, or which obstructs or impedes the
free passage of pedestrians or public travel upon such sidewalk, street, alley
or public place, or any portion thereof, shall be deemed in violation of this
chapter. (1990 Code §6-606)
   B.   It shall be unlawful for any person to cast, keep or leave upon any of
the streets, highways, alleys or public grounds within the corporate limits of
the City any manure, stagnant or impure water, refuse, vegetables, decayed or
decaying substances, slops, swill, garbage, scrap iron, junk, car bodies or
filth of any kind, the same of which are hereby declared to be a nuisance and a
violation of this chapter. (1990 Code §6-607)
3-1-7: TRASH AND JUNK ON PRIVATE PROPERTY; ABATEMENT:
   A.   Prohibition: It shall be unlawful for any person to permit or suffer to
accumulate in or upon any yard, lot, place or premises owned or occupied by
him, or for which he may be the agent, within the corporate limits of the City,
any manure, stagnant or impure water, refuse, vegetables, decayed or decaying
substances, slops, swill, garbage, scrap iron, junk, car bodies or filth of any
kind, or permit or suffer such yard, lot, place or premises to be or remain in
such condition as to cause or create a noisome or offensive smell or
atmosphere, and the existence of such condition is hereby declared to be a
nuisance and a violation of this chapter. Provided, that no person shall be
prosecuted for a violation of this subsection unless such violation continues
for twenty four (24) hours after he has received the notice provided in
subsection B of this section. (1990 Code §6-608)
   B.   Notice And Abatement: Whenever the City shall have been informed of the
violation of any of the provisions of subsection A of this section, he shall
immediately make or cause to be made an examination of the yard, lot, place or
premises on which it is charged that such violation is suffered or permitted,
and if it is found that there is such a violation, he shall forthwith give or
cause to be given, to either the owner, agent or occupant of such yard, lot,
place or premises or to all of them, a notice in writing to abate such nuisance
and to remove such manure, stagnant or impure water, refuse, vegetables,
decayed or decaying substances, slops, swill, garbage, scrap iron, junk, car
bodies, or filth of any kind, and if the same is not so removed within twenty
four (24) hours after such notice, the Lewis County Sheriff shall cause the
owner, occupant, or agent of such premises to be arrested, and if he shall be
convicted, shall cause the same to be removed, and the expenses of the removal
thereof shall be paid by the City in the first instance, but the same shall be
taxed as part of the costs in such prosecution. (1990 Code §6-609)
CHAPTER 2
WEEDS
SECTION:
3-2-1: Definition; Prohibition
3-2-2: Owner Or Occupant Responsibility
3-2-3: Removal By City; Cost Assessment
3-2-1: DEFINITION; PROHIBITION:
   A.   Weeds, within the meaning of this chapter, includes all vegetable
growth that is unsightly, troublesome, useless or noxious.
   B.   All weed and vegetable growth that has been declared noxious,
destructive or detrimental to the agricultural interests shall be completely
and effectually destroyed. It shall be a sufficient compliance with this
chapter if all other kinds not so declared noxious are kept closely cut to the
ground. (1990 Code §9-401)
3-2-2: OWNER OR OCCUPANT RESPONSIBILITY:
All owners or occupants of any lot, block or subdivision of land are hereby
required to cut and remove all weeds therefrom. The said persons shall also
remove all weeds up to the center of the street or alley, along, in front of,
or abutting said premises and to keep the same free from weeds. (1990 Code §9-
401)
3-2-3: REMOVAL BY CITY; COST ASSESSMENT:
Whenever the growth of weeds advances to or becomes in a condition prohibited
by this chapter, the City or any of its officers shall notify such owner or
occupant to remove such growth and, in default of this being done, the City
shall remove and cut such weeds or do any other work necessary to place said
premises in good condition. The Clerk-Treasurer shall then certify the cost of
the same and the cost therein occurred shall be a lien upon the property. (1990
Code §9-401)
CHAPTER 3
FIREWORKS AND EXPLOSIVES
SECTION:
3-3-1: Fireworks
3-3-2: Transportation Of Explosives
3-3-1: FIREWORKS:
   A.   Definition: The term "pyrotechnics" shall mean any sparkler, squib,
rocket, firecracker, roman candle, fire balloon, signal light, railroad track
torpedo, flashlight composition, pistol, cane, cannon or other appliances using
blank cartridges or caps, fireworks or other devices or compositions used to
obtain visible or audible pyrotechnic displays. (1990 Code §7-201)
   B.   Fireworks Prohibited; Exceptions: No person, firm or corporation shall,
within the City, have, keep, store, use, manufacture, sell or offer for sale,
handle or transport any pyrotechnics; provided, however:
      1.   That nothing in this section shall be held to apply to the
possession or use of signaling devices for current daily consumption by
railroads, trucks, and others requiring them.
      2.   That the Chief of the Fire Department or the Clerk-Treasurer may,
upon due application, issue a permit to a properly qualified person for giving
a pyrotechnic display of fireworks in the public parks or other open places.
(1990 Code §7-202)
3-3-2: TRANSPORTATION OF EXPLOSIVES:
   A.   Explosives shall not be transported or carried on or in any conveyance
carrying passengers for hire. (1990 Code §7-301)
   B.   Every vehicle, while carrying explosives, shall be marked or placarded
on each side and the rear with the word "explosives" in letters not less than
eight inches (8") high, and there shall be displayed on the rear of the vehicle
a red flag not less than twenty four inches (24") square, marked with the word
"danger" in white letters six inches (6") high. Also, the vehicle shall be
equipped with not less than two (2) fire extinguishers, filled and ready for
immediate use, and placed at a convenient point on the vehicle. (1990 Code §7-
301; amd. 2018 Code)
   C.   It shall be unlawful for any person in charge of a vehicle containing
explosives to smoke in, upon or near such vehicle; to drive, load or unload the
vehicle while intoxicated; to drive the vehicle in a careless or reckless
manner, or to unload such vehicle in a careless or reckless manner.
   D.   It shall be unlawful for any person to place or carry, or cause to be
placed or carried, any metal tool or other similar piece of metal, in the bed
or body of a vehicle containing explosives.
   E.   It shall be unlawful for any person to place or carry or cause to be
placed or carried, in the bed or body of a vehicle containing explosives, any
exploders, detonators, blasting caps, or other similar explosive material, or
to carry in or upon any such vehicle any matches. (1990 Code §7-301)
CHAPTER 4
FIRE PREVENTION AND PROTECTION
SECTION:
3-4-1: Smoking Prohibited Under Certain Conditions
3-4-2: Bonfires And Outdoor Rubbish Fires
3-4-3: Lighting Fire Upon Land Of Others
3-4-4: Deposits Of Hot Ashes And Other Dangerous Materials
3-4-5: Accumulating Waste Materials
3-4-6: Handling Of Combustible Materials
3-4-7: Storage Of Combustible Materials; Permit
3-4-8: Flammable Decorative Materials In Stores
3-4-9: Safe Condition Of Chimneys And Heating Appliances
3-4-10: Paint Removal With Torches Or Flame Producing Devices
3-4-11: Fire Protection Equipment
3-4-12: Fire Hazard Inspection Authorized
3-4-1: SMOKING PROHIBITED UNDER CERTAIN CONDITIONS:
   A.   Definition: The term "smoking" shall mean and include the carrying of
lighted pipe, vaping devices, cigarette or tobacco in any form. (1990 Code §7-
701; amd. 2018 Code)
   B.   Designation Of No Smoking Areas:
      1.   Where conditions are such as to make smoking a hazard in any areas
of warehouses, stores, industrial plants, institutions, places of assembly, and
in open spaces where combustible materials are stored or handled, the Chief of
the Fire Department is empowered and authorized to order the owner or occupant
in writing to post "No Smoking" signs in each building, structure, room or
place in which smoking shall be prohibited.
      2.   The Chief of the Fire Department shall designate specific safe
locations, if necessary, in any building, structure or place in which smoking
may be permitted. (1990 Code §7-702)
   C.   No Smoking Signs: "No Smoking" signs required in accordance with
subsection B of this section shall read "By Order of the Chief of the Fire
Department". (1990 Code §7-703)
   D.   Prohibited Acts: It shall be unlawful for any person to remove any
legally required "No Smoking" sign or to smoke in any place where such signs
are posted. (1990 Code §7-704)
3-4-2: BONFIRES AND OUTDOOR RUBBISH FIRES:
   A.   Permit Required: No person shall kindle or maintain any bonfire or
rubbish fire or authorize any such fire to be kindled or maintained on or in
any public street, alley, road or other public ground without a permit or other
proper authorization.
   B.   Location Restricted: No person shall kindle or maintain any bonfire or
rubbish fire or authorize any such fire to be kindled or maintained on any
private land unless: 1) the location is not less than fifty feet (50') from any
structure and adequate provision is made to prevent fire from spreading to
within fifty feet (50') of any structure; or 2) the fire is contained in an
approved waste burner with closed top, located safely not less than fifteen
feet (15') from any structure. (1990 Code §7-501)
   C.   Authority Of Chief: The Chief of the Fire Department may prohibit,
restrict or require a permit for any or all bonfires and outdoor rubbish fires
when atmospheric conditions or local circumstances make such fires hazardous.
(1990 Code §7-501; amd. 2018 Code)
3-4-3: LIGHTING FIRE UPON LAND OF OTHERS:
No person shall kindle a fire upon the land of another without permission of
the owner thereof or his agent. (1990 Code §7-502)
3-4-4: DEPOSITS OF HOT ASHES AND OTHER DANGEROUS MATERIALS:
No person shall deposit hot ashes or cinders, or smoldering coals, or greasy or
oily substances liable to spontaneous ignition, into any wooden receptacle, or
place the same within ten feet (10') of any combustible materials, except in
metal or other noncombustible receptacles. Such receptacles, unless resting on
a noncombustible floor or on the ground outside the building, shall be placed
on noncombustible stands, and in every case must be kept at least two feet (2')
away from any combustible wall or partition. (1990 Code §7-503)
3-4-5: ACCUMULATING WASTE MATERIALS:
Accumulations of waste paper, hay, grass, straw, weeds, litter or combustible
or flammable waste or rubbish of any kind shall not be permitted to remain upon
any roof or in any court, yard, vacant lot or open space. All weeds, grass,
vines or other growth, when same endangers property, or is liable to be fired,
shall be cut down and removed by the owner or occupant of the property upon
which same is located. (1990 Code §7-504)
3-4-6: HANDLING OF COMBUSTIBLE MATERIALS:
   A.   No person making, using, storing or having in his charge, or under his
control any shavings, excelsior, rubbish, sacks, bags, litter, hay, straw or
combustible waste materials shall fail or neglect at the close of each day to
cause all such material which is not compactly baled and stacked in an orderly
manner to be removed from the building or stored in suitable vaults or in metal
or metal lined, covered, receptacles or bins.
   B.   The Chief of the Fire Department shall require suitable baling presses
to be installed in stores, apartment buildings, factories and similar places
where accumulations of paper and waste materials are not removed at least every
second day. (1990 Code §7-505)
3-4-7: STORAGE OF COMBUSTIBLE MATERIALS; PERMIT:
   A.   Permit Required: No person shall store in excess of two thousand five
hundred (2,500) cubic feet gross volume of combustible empty packing cases,
boxes, barrels or similar containers, or rubber tires, or baled cotton, rubber
or cork, or other similarly combustible material without a permit from the
Chief of the Fire Department.
   B.   Storage Requirements: Storage in buildings shall be orderly, shall not
be within two feet (2') of the ceiling, and not so located as to endanger exit
from the building. Storage in the open shall not be more than twenty feet (20')
in height, shall be so located, with respect to adjacent buildings, as not to
constitute a hazard, and shall be compact and orderly. (1990 Code §7-506)
3-4-8: FLAMMABLE DECORATIVE MATERIALS IN STORES:
Cotton batting, straw, dry vines, leaves, trees, or other highly flammable
materials shall not be used for decorative purposes in show windows or other
parts of stores unless flameproofed; provided, however, that nothing in this
section shall be held to prohibit the display of saleable goods permitted and
offered for sale. (1990 Code §7-507)
3-4-9: SAFE CONDITION OF CHIMNEYS AND HEATING APPLIANCES:
   A.   All chimneys, smokestacks or similar devices for conveying smoke or hot
gases to the outer air and the stoves, furnaces, fire boxes or boilers to which
they are connected shall be constructed and maintained in such a manner as not
to create a fire hazard.
   B.   To have any combustible substance such as wood, paper or cloth of any
kind nearer than three inches (3") of any stove, furnace, fireplace or range or
pipe as a permanent fixture in any building in the City is hereby prohibited.
(1990 Code §7-508)
3-4-10: PAINT REMOVAL WITH TORCHES OR FLAME PRODUCING DEVICES:
Any person using a torch or other flame producing device for removing paint
from any building or structure shall provide one approved fire extinguisher or
water hose connected to the water supply on the premises where such burning is
done. In all cases, the person doing the burning shall remain on the premises
one hour after the torch or flame producing device has been used. (1990 Code
§7-509)
3-4-11: FIRE PROTECTION EQUIPMENT:
   A.   Chief Survey Premises; Specify Needed Equipment: The Chief of the Fire
Department shall survey each mercantile and manufacturing establishment,
school, place of assembly, place of detention, hotel and multi-family house,
and shall specify suitable fire detecting devices or extinguishing appliances
which shall be provided, in or near boiler rooms, kitchens of restaurants,
clubs and like establishments, storage rooms involving considerable combustible
material, rooms in which hazardous manufacturing processes are involved, garage
sections, and other places of a generally hazardous nature. Such devices or
appliances may consist of automatic fire alarm systems, automatic sprinkler or
water spray systems, standpipe and hose, fixed or portable fire extinguishers
of a type suitable for the probable class of fire, or suitable asbestos
blankets, manual or automatic covers, or carbon dioxide or other inert gas
extinguishing systems. In specially hazardous processes or storages, appliances
of more than one type or special systems may be required. (1990 Code §7-601)
   B.   Maintenance Of Equipment: Sprinkler systems, standpipe systems, fire
alarm systems, and other fire protective or extinguishing systems or appliances
which have been installed in compliance with any permit or order, or because of
any law or ordinance shall be maintained in operative condition at all times,
and it shall be unlawful for any owner or occupant to reduce the effectiveness
of the protection required; except, that this shall not prohibit the owner or
occupant from temporarily reducing or discontinuing the protection where
necessary to make tests, repairs, alterations or additions. The Chief of the
Fire Department shall be notified before such tests, repairs, alterations or
additions are started unless the work is to be continuous until completion.
(1990 Code §7-602)
3-4-12: FIRE HAZARD INSPECTION AUTHORIZED:
   A.   Fire Chief May Inspect: Authority is hereby given to the Chief of the
Fire Department to inspect or cause to be inspected by the Fire Department
officers or members, as often as may be necessary, all buildings, premises and
public thoroughfares, except the interior of private dwellings, for the purpose
of ascertaining and causing to be corrected any conditions liable to cause
fire, or any violations of the provisions or intent of any laws of the City
affecting the fire hazard. (1990 Code §7-801)
   B.   Hazard Removal Upon Order Of Chief: Whenever an officer or member shall
find in any building, upon any premises or other place, combustible matter or
dangerous accumulation of rubbish or unnecessary accumulation of waste paper,
boxes, shavings, or any other highly inflammable materials especially liable to
fire, and which is so situated as to endanger property, or shall find
obstruction to or on fire escapes, stairs, passageways, doors or windows liable
to interfere with the operation of the Fire Department, or egress of occupants
in case of fire, he shall order the same to be removed or remedied, and such
order shall forthwith be complied with by the owner or occupant of such
premises or buildings, subject to appeal within twenty four (24) hours to the
City Council, who shall within five (5) days review such order and file its
decision thereon, and, unless the order is revoked or modified, it shall remain
in full force and be obeyed by such owner or occupant. (1990 Code §7-802)
   C.   Failure To Remove Hazard: Any owner or occupant failing to comply with
such order within ten (10) days after the service of said order shall be deemed
guilty of a misdemeanor. (1990 Code §7-803)
   D.   Serving Of Order: The service of any such order shall be made upon the
occupant of the premises to whom it is directed by either delivering a true
copy of the same to such occupant personally or by delivering same to and
leaving it with any person in charge of the premises, or in case no such
persons are found upon the premises, by affixing a copy thereof in a
conspicuous place on the door to the entrance of the said premises. Whenever it
may be necessary to serve such an order upon the owner of the premises, such
order may be served either by delivering to and leaving with said person a true
copy of the said order, or if such owner is absent from the jurisdiction of the
officer making the order, by mailing him such copy to the owner's last known
post office address. (1990 Code §7-804)
TITLE 4
LAW ENFORCEMENT AND PUBLIC SAFETY
CHAPTER 1
LAW ENFORCEMENT
SECTION:
4-1-1: Enforcement By County
4-1-1: ENFORCEMENT BY COUNTY:
The City hereby appoints the Sheriff of Lewis County and his duly appointed
deputies as police officers for the City, with all of the powers and duties as
provided by law for such police officers within the territorial jurisdiction of
the incorporated limits of the City, as they now or shall hereafter encompass.
(1990 Code §3-101)
CHAPTER 2
VOLUNTEER FIRE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
4-2-1: Department Created; Supervision
4-2-2: Definitions
4-2-3: Department Officers
4-2-4: Social Officers
4-2-5: Duties Of Chief
4-2-6: Duties Of Assistant Chief, Captain
4-2-7: Membership; Authority
4-2-8: Compensation
4-2-9: Equipment
4-2-10: Mutual Aid Agreements
4-2-11: General Requirements And Restrictions
4-2-12: Violations; Enforcement
4-2-1: DEPARTMENT CREATED; SUPERVISION:
A department to be hereinafter known as the Winchester Volunteer Fire
Department, the object of which shall be prevention of fire and protection of
life and property within the City limits, is hereby created. The Fire
Department shall be a division of the Department of Public Protection and shall
be under the supervision of the City Council. (Ord. 266, 2-2013; amd. 2018
Code)
4-2-2: DEFINITIONS:
Unless the context specifically indicates otherwise, the meanings of terms used
in this chapter shall be as follows:
CITY: The City of Winchester, Idaho.
COUNCIL OR CITY COUNCIL: The City Council of Winchester, Idaho.
DEPARTMENT: The Winchester Volunteer Fire Department.
FIRE CHIEF: The appointed Chief of the Winchester Volunteer Fire Department.
(Ord. 266, 2-2013)
4-2-3: DEPARTMENT OFFICERS:
   A.   Composition: The department shall consist of a Chief, an Assistant
Chief, a Captain, a Secretary, a Treasurer, and such other officers as the
Chief and the City Council may deem necessary for the effective operations of
the department.
   B.   Chief Of Department:
      1.   The Volunteer Fire Department shall elect from their own membership,
a person to be recommended to the City Council for appointment as Chief of the
Department. The person chosen shall be elected by a majority of the membership
of the department present and voting at said election. The person so
recommended shall, upon confirmation and approval of the City Council, be
appointed by the Council as Chief of the Department. The Chief shall be
technically qualified by training and experiences and shall have the ability to
command men and women, and hold their respect and confidence.
      2.   The Chief shall serve for a term of two (2) years and may be, from
time to time, re-recommended and re-appointed.
      3.   The Chief shall be accountable to the City Council only, and shall
make written and verbal reports thereto as the Council may require.
      4.   The Chief cannot be removed from the office during his term except
by a written notice served upon the Fire Chief setting forth the grounds and
charges against him, the grounds and charges may be preferred by the City
Council, or by a majority of the membership of the Volunteer Fire Department,
and then the said Fire Chief cannot be removed unless he shall have a hearing
with the right to defend himself against the charges and a vote of a majority
of the members of the City Council.
   C.   Selection Of Officers; Removal; Terms: The Assistant Chiefs, Captain,
and all other departmental officers except the Chief shall be elected by the
members of the Volunteer Fire Department from its own membership and said
persons shall be chosen by a majority vote of members present and voting at
said election and shall be accountable to the Chief and subject to removal by
majority vote of the members of the Volunteer Fire Department. The Assistant
Chiefs, Captain, and all other departmental officers shall be elected for a
term of two (2) years. (Ord. 266, 2-2013)
4-2-4: SOCIAL OFFICERS:
   A.   The department may elect a President, Vice President, Secretary and
Treasurer, to be known as Social Officers. Such officers may be elected in any
manner and for any term the membership may decide upon, and their duties shall
be to arrange for and manage any or all social functions sponsored by the
department.
   B.   The functions and duties of said Social Officers shall in no way
interfere with those of the regular department officers who are charged with
responsibility for all fire service activities of the department. (Ord. 266, 2-
2013)
4-2-5: DUTIES OF CHIEF:
   A.   The Chief shall be responsible to the City Council for the personnel,
morale, and general efficiency of the department.
   B.   The Chief shall, at least twice monthly, conduct suitable drills and
instruction in the operation and handling of equipment; first aid in rescue
work, salvage, a study of the buildings in the City, fire prevention, water
supplies and all other matters generally considered essential to good
firemanship and safety of life and property from fire. When weather conditions
do not permit drills, meetings shall consist of discussion of firefighting
equipment and apparatus.
   C.   The Chief is hereby required to assist the proper authorities in
suppressing the crime of arson by investigating or causing to be investigated
the cause, origin and circumstances of all fires.
   D.   The Chief is hereby empowered to enter any and all buildings and
premises at any reasonable hour for the purposes of making inspections and to
serve written notice upon the owner or occupant to abate, within a specified
time, any and all fire hazards that may be found.
Any person so served with a notice to abate any fire hazards shall comply
therewith and promptly notify the Chief.
   E.   The Chief shall see that complete records are kept of all fires,
inspections, apparatus and minor equipment, personnel and other information
about the work of the department.
   F.   The Chief shall report quarterly to the City Council the condition of
the apparatus and equipment; the number of fires during the quarter, their
location and cause, the date of same and the loss occasioned thereby, the
number and purpose of all other runs made; the number of members responding to
each fire or other run and any changes in membership.
   G.   The Chief shall make a complete annual report to the City Council at
the last meeting at the close of the fiscal year, such report to include the
information specified in subsection F of this section, together with
comparative data for previous years and recommendations for improving the
effectiveness of the department.
   H.   The Chief of the Fire Department shall be the Chief Executive Officer
of the department, subject to the rules and regulations and orders of the Fire
Department and the City Council and shall have under such conditions control
and command of all property belonging to the department and of all subordinates
in the service. He shall enforce the faithful observance of the ordinances of
the City, and the rules and regulations of the Fire Department.
   I.   It shall be the duty of the Chief of the Fire Department to see that
all property and apparatus provided for the use of the Fire Department is
protected from violence and kept clean, and in good repair for immediate use.
   J.   At all fires, the Chief of the Fire Department shall have sole command
and all members of the Fire Department and the County Sheriff and his duly
appointed deputies shall, during the continuance of any fire, be subject to his
order. He may, when deemed necessary for extinguishment of any fire, call to
his aid any person present, and it shall be the duty of every person so called
upon by the Chief of the Fire Department to render him prompt service;
provided, however, that in the absence of the Chief or Assistant Chiefs or
Captain, the first fire personnel to arrive upon the scene of said fire shall
be in command therewith until the arrival of the Chief or Assistant Chiefs or
superior officer in the Fire Department. (Ord. 266, 2-2013)
4-2-6: DUTIES OF ASSISTANT CHIEF, CAPTAIN:
   A.   The Assistant Chief and Captain shall report to the Chief at fires and
assist him in the discharge of his duties.
   B.   In the absence of the Chief, the Assistant Chief shall command the
department and be held responsible therefor in all respects with the full
powers and responsibilities of the Chief.
   C.   In the absence of both the Chief and Assistant Chief, the Captain shall
command the department with the full powers and responsibilities of the Chief.
(Ord. 266, 2-2013)
4-2-7: MEMBERSHIP; AUTHORITY:
   A.   The membership of the department shall consist of as many able bodied
individuals who live in or around the City within a reasonable travel distance
as possible. The department resources shall be the limiting factor in
membership size.
   B.   Any member of the department may be suspended or discharged from the
department on charges preferred by the Chief to the membership of the
department at any time the Chief may deem such action necessary for the good of
the department, and at a regular meeting, shall vote by secret ballot to
discharge such member from membership.
   C.   The Volunteer Fire Department is hereby authorized to adopt bylaws,
rules and regulations for the administration of the department not in conflict
with the laws of the State or the ordinances of the City. These bylaws, rules
and regulations shall be effective when approved by the City Council and a copy
filed with the City Clerk-Treasurer. The membership of the Volunteer Fire
Department shall, within thirty (30) days after the effective date hereof,
adopt a set of bylaws, rules and regulations for the department. (Ord. 266, 2-
2013)
4-2-8: COMPENSATION:
The compensation to be paid by the City to the Fire Department shall be in
addition to such other compensations elsewhere granted in other ordinances of
the City, as follows:
   A.   The Fire Department shall receive for each member attending each drill
or lecture meeting the sum of fifty cents ($0.50). Attendance shall be
determined by roll call by the Secretary or Treasurer forthwith after the
meeting has been called to order. The department shall receive no compensation
for members not present at said drill or meeting.
   B.   For services when actually engaged in fighting fires or when responding
to a fire alarm, the department shall receive one dollar ($1.00) for each
member who actually engages in firefighting or responds to a fire alarm. (Ord.
266, 2-2013)
4-2-9: EQUIPMENT:
   A.   The department shall be equipped with the firefighting apparatus and
equipment as the City now owns and that which may be acquired from time to time
to maintain its efficiency and properly protect life and property from fire.
   B.   Recommendations of apparatus and equipment needed shall be made by the
Chief and, after approval by the City Council, shall be purchased in such
manner as may be designated by the City Council. (Ord. 266, 2-2013)
   C.   All equipment of the department shall be safely and conveniently housed
in such places as may be designated by the Fire Chief.
   D.   No person shall use any fire apparatus or equipment for any private
purpose without proper authority nor shall they take away or conceal any
article used in any way by the department.
   E.   No person shall enter any place where fire apparatus is housed or
handle any apparatus or equipment belonging to the department unless
accompanied by, or having special permission of, any officer or authorized
member of the department.
(Ord. 266, 2-2013; amd. 2018 Code)
4-2-10: MUTUAL AID AGREEMENTS:
   A.   The Fire Department of the City is hereby authorized to enter into
agreements or contracts with nearby incorporated City, County, State, Tribal,
or Federal agencies in the establishment of a mutual aid system. All contracts
and agreements shall have the proper approval of the City Council before they
shall become effective.
   B.   The department shall respond to all incidents in accordance with an
established Response Guideline mutually approved by both the City Council and
the department. This protocol may be revised as necessary to best protect the
City, but has full force of this chapter and department. (Ord. 266, 2-2013)
4-2-11: GENERAL REQUIREMENTS AND RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Right-Of-Way: All emergency vehicles shall have the right- of-way over
all other traffic when responding to an alarm, in accordance with State traffic
laws.
   B.   Driving Over Fire Hose: No person shall drive any vehicle over a fire
hose except upon specific orders from the Chief or other officers in charge
where the hose is used.
   C.   Parking Near Fire Station Or Fire Hydrant: No person shall park any
vehicle or otherwise cause any obstruction to be placed within twenty feet
(20') of the entrance to any fire station or other place where fire apparatus
is stored, or within fifteen feet (15') of any fire hydrant or cistern.
   D.   Following Fire Apparatus; Parking Near Fire: No unauthorized person
with any vehicle shall follow within five hundred feet (500') of any apparatus
belonging to the department, nor park any vehicle within five hundred feet
(500') of a fire.
   E.   False Alarm: No person shall maliciously turn in or cause to be turned
in a false alarm. (Ord. 266, 2-2013; amd. 2018 Code)
4-2-12: VIOLATIONS; ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Any person violating the provisions of subsections
4-2-5D,
4-2-9D and E, and
4-2-11C, D, and E of this chapter shall be referred to the Lewis County
Sheriff's Office for prosecution according to applicable State laws.
   B.   All regularly appointed members of the department are hereby given the
necessary special police powers for the purpose of enforcing the provisions of
this chapter. (Ord. 266, 2-2013)
CHAPTER 3
GENERAL OFFENSES
SECTION:
4-3-1: Aid In Breach Of Peace
4-3-2: Aid To An Offense
4-3-3: Assault Or Battery
4-3-4: Disorderly Conduct
4-3-5: Disturbing The Peace
4-3-6: Drunkenness
4-3-7: Obscenity; Lewd Conduct
4-3-8: Prostitution; House Of Prostitution
4-3-9: False Pretenses
4-3-10: False Representation
4-3-11: Fraudulently Avoiding Payment Of Admission Fees
4-3-12: Gambling
4-3-13: Resisting An Officer
4-3-14: Offenses Concerning Prisoners
4-3-15: Keeping Of Junk Restricted
4-3-16: Abandoned Refrigerators, Other Containers
4-3-17: Deposits Of Injurious Materials On Thoroughfares
4-3-18: Malicious Injury To Property
4-3-19: Riot
4-3-20: Unlawful Assembly
4-3-21: Noise
4-3-22: Radio And Television Interference
4-3-23: Weapons And Firearms; Shooting Galleries
4-3-24: Trespassing
4-3-25: Vagrancy
4-3-1: AID IN BREACH OF PEACE:
Any person who shall aid or countenance in making any improper noise, riot or
breach of the peace or diversion in the streets or elsewhere within the City to
the annoyance or disturbance of citizens or travelers shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor. (1990 Code §6-101)
4-3-2: AID TO AN OFFENSE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to in any way or manner, aid, abet,
counsel, advise or encourage any other person in the commission of any of the
acts mentioned herein, or in any manner encourage the commission of such
offense hereby defined. (1990 Code §6-103)
4-3-3: ASSAULT OR BATTERY:
   A.   Definitions: For the purpose of this section, the following terms shall
have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection:
   ASSAULT: An unlawful attempt, coupled with a present ability, to commit a
violent injury on the person of another.
   BATTERY: Any willful and unlawful use of force or violence upon the person
of another.
   B.   Prohibited Acts: It shall be unlawful for any person to commit assault
or battery. (1990 Code §6-105)
4-3-4: DISORDERLY CONDUCT:
It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in any illegal or improper
diversion, or to use insulting, indecent or immoral language, to be guilty of
any incident, insulting or immoral conduct or behavior. (1990 Code §6-108)
4-3-5: DISTURBING THE PEACE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to disturb the peace, quiet or order by
violent, tumultuous or offensive conduct or acts or by unseemly, profane,
obscene or offensive language calculated to provoke a breach of the peace, and
any person who shall permit any such conduct in or upon any house or premises
owned by or controlled by him so that others in the vicinity are disturbed
thereby, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. (1990 Code §6-110)
4-3-6: DRUNKENNESS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to be found drunk, intoxicated or under the
influence of intoxicating liquor upon any public thoroughfare or other public
place. (1990 Code §6-111)
4-3-7: OBSCENITY; LEWD CONDUCT:
   A.   Distribution Of Obscene Literature: It shall be unlawful for any person
to exhibit, pass, give or deliver to another any obscene, lewd or indecent
book, pamphlet, picture, card, print, paper, writing, mold, cast or figure, or
to have same in his possession, unless it be shown that the possession is for
lawful purposes. (1990 Code §6-109)
   B.   Indecent Exposure: It shall be unlawful for any person to appear in a
state of nudity in any public place, or in any such place to make any indecent
exposure of his or her person or private parts thereof, or the private parts of
another, or to conduct himself or herself in a lewd or lascivious manner. (1990
Code §6-120)
   C.   Lewd Or Obscene Conduct: It shall be unlawful for any person to write
or print any lewd or obscene language or to draw any lewd or obscene pictures
on any building, wall, fence, railing or other place where it may be seen or
read by others. (1990 Code §6-122)
   D.   Obscene Conduct: It shall be unlawful for any person to urinate or
stool in any place open to public view, or to be guilty of any lewd, lascivious
or obscene conduct, or to sing any lewd or obscene song, ballad or other words
in any public place, or any other place where other persons are present. (1990
Code §6-124)
4-3-8: PROSTITUTION; HOUSE OF PROSTITUTION:
   A.   Any person who pursues or advertises her vocation as a prostitute, and
every person who advertises the vocation of a prostitute or solicits for a
prostitute, and every person guilty of prostitution, upon conviction thereof,
shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor.
   B.   Every person who keeps or assists in the keeping of a house of ill fame
or prostitution, or who knowingly resides therein or who knowingly rents,
leases or permits any person to occupy any house or room owned, leased or
controlled by him, to use for this purpose, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor.
(1990 Code §6-125)
4-3-9: FALSE PRETENSES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to obtain any food, drink, goods, wares, or
merchandise under false pretenses, or to enter any public place and call for
refreshments, or food or other articles and receive the same and refuse to pay
for the same, or depart without paying for same or satisfying the person from
whom he received the food, refreshments, goods, wares or merchandise. (1990
Code §6-114)
4-3-10: FALSE REPRESENTATION:
It shall be unlawful for any person to falsely represent himself to be an
officer of the City, or to attempt to impersonate any such officer, or, without
authority, perform any official act therein on behalf of an officer. (1990 Code
§6-115)
4-3-11: FRAUDULENTLY AVOIDING PAYMENT OF ADMISSION FEES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to fraudulently enter without payment of
the proper admission fees any theater, ballroom, lecture, concert, or other
place where admission fees are charged; provided, however, that nothing herein
contained shall be deemed to prohibit or restrict the free admission of police
officers engaged in the performance of police duties, to any place of public
entertainment or amusement. (1990 Code §6-116)
4-3-12: GAMBLING:
It shall be unlawful for any person to deal, play, or conduct, either as owner,
employee or lessee, whether for hire or not, any games of faro, monte,
roulette, lansquenet, rouge et noir, rondo, Indian stick game, or any game
played with cards, dice or any other device for money, checks, credit or other
representative of value. (1990 Code §6-118)
4-3-13: RESISTING AN OFFICER:
It shall be unlawful for any person to interfere with, resist, delay, obstruct,
molest or threaten to molest any officer of the City in the exercise of his
official duties. (1990 Code §6-126)
4-3-14: OFFENSES CONCERNING PRISONERS:
   A.   Aid In Escape: It shall be unlawful for any person to aid or assist any
person to escape from lawful confinement, or to assist any person to escape
from the custody of any peace officer. (1990 Code §6-102)
   B.   Escape From Custody: It shall be unlawful for any person convicted of
any offense or in lawful custody to escape or attempt to escape from custody.
(1990 Code §6-112)
   C.   Furnishing Weapons And Other Articles To Prisoners: It shall be
unlawful for any person to furnish, or attempt to furnish, or take into jail,
or to deliver, or attempt to deliver, to any prisoner therein confined, or in
the custody of any officer, any weapon, tool, intoxicating liquors, drug or
other article without the consent of the officer in charge. (1990 Code §6-117)
4-3-15: KEEPING OF JUNK RESTRICTED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to store or keep any old articles or
materials which may be classed as junk, adjacent to or in close proximity to
any school house, church, public park, public grounds, business buildings or
residence without first providing proper and tight buildings for the storage of
the same. (1990 Code §6-121)
4-3-16: ABANDONED REFRIGERATORS, OTHER CONTAINERS:
It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to leave or permit to
remain outside any dwelling, building or other structure or within any
unoccupied or abandoned building, dwelling or other structure under his control
in a place accessible to children, or to deposit in the City refuse disposal
dump, any abandoned, unattended or discarded icebox, refrigerator or other
container which has a door, lid, snap lock or other locking device which may
not be released from the inside without first removing said door, lid, snap
lock or other locking device, or by first fastening, bolting or locking the
same in such a manner that it is impossible to open the same by the use of the
hands. (1990 Code §6-401)
4-3-17: DEPOSITS OF INJURIOUS MATERIALS ON THOROUGHFARES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to deposit, place or allow to remain in or
upon public thoroughfares any material or substances injurious to person or
property. (1990 Code §6-107)
4-3-18: MALICIOUS INJURY TO PROPERTY:
It shall be unlawful for any person to wilfully and maliciously injure, deface,
mutilate, remove, pull down, break or in any manner interfere with or molest or
secrete or destroy any real or personal property belonging to or under the
control of any person. (1990 Code §6-123)
4-3-19: RIOT:
It shall be unlawful when two (2) or more persons assemble for the purpose of
disturbing the peace or for the purpose of committing any unlawful act or for
any such person to fail or refuse to immediately disperse upon an order to do
so by a police officer. It shall be unlawful for any person, except public
officers and persons assisting in preserving the peace, to remain present at
the place of such riot, rout or unlawful assembly. (1990 Code §6-127)
4-3-20: UNLAWFUL ASSEMBLY:
It shall be unlawful for two (2) or more persons to assembly together for the
purpose of disturbing the peace or for the purpose of committing an unlawful
act, and to not disperse upon the command of an officer so to do. (1990 Code
§6-130)
4-3-21: NOISE:
   A.   Purpose; Council Authority: The purpose of this section is the
protection of health, safety and welfare of the residents of the City. It is
determined that sound can and does constitute a hazard to the health, safety,
welfare and the quality of life of the residents of the City. The Mayor and
Council, by way of Idaho Code section 50-308, are empowered to impose
reasonable limitations and regulations upon the production of sound to reduce
the harmful effect thereof.
   B.   Definition: "Loud or offensive noise" is that which is plainly audible
within any place of residence, business, hospital, farm property with animals
or restaurants other than the source of the sound, or upon a public right-of-
way or street at a distance of one hundred feet (100') or more from the source
of the sound.
   C.   Public Noise Prohibited: Between the hours of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M.
one day and seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. the next day, it shall be unlawful for
any person or business to make, cause, or allow loud or offensive noise by
means of voice, musical instrument, horn, radio, loudspeaker, automobile,
machinery or other sound amplifying equipment or any other means which disturbs
the peace, quiet and comfort of any reasonable person of normal sensitiveness
residing in the area.
   D.   Violation A Misdemeanor: Any person violating this section shall be
guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord. 283, 11-2-2017)
4-3-22: RADIO AND TELEVISION INTERFERENCE:
   A.   Interference Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any person knowingly
to operate, cause to be operated or permit the operation of any wire for
carrying electric energy or any fixtures, machine, device, apparatus or other
instrument, the operation of which shall cause reasonable preventable
electrical interference with radio or television reception. (1990 Code §4-201)
   B.   Inspection: The City Clerk-Treasurer or the County Sheriff or any other
designated person of the City, shall have the right at any reasonable hour to
enter upon and into any premises for the purpose of inspecting or locating any
wires, fixtures, machines, devices, apparatus, or other instruments which are
or may be kept or operated in violation of the provisions of this section.
Should any inspection disclose that any equipment described in this section be
defective, then the Clerk-Treasurer shall notify in writing the owner or
occupant of said premises, or the operator of said equipment, of the defects
and suggest steps to be taken to remedy such defects. Upon receipt of such
written notice, such owner, occupant or operator shall forthwith take effective
steps to remedy such defects. (1990 Code §4-202; amd. 2018 Code)
4-3-23: WEAPONS AND FIREARMS; SHOOTING GALLERIES:
   A.   Definition: Whenever the term "firearms" is used in this section, the
term shall mean any instrument used in the propulsion of shot, shell or bullets
or other harmful objects by the action of gunpowder exploded within it, or by
the action of compressed air within it, or by the power of springs and
including what are commonly known as air rifles and BB guns. (1990 Code §6-201)
   B.   Concealed Weapons: Concealed weapons regulations shall be in accordance
with State Statute. (2018 Code)
   C.   Discharge Of Firearms: It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge
firearms of any kind or description within the limits of the City; provided,
however, that this shall not apply to police officers in the discharge of their
duties. (1990 Code §6-203)
   D.   Shooting Galleries Or Gun Clubs: The City Council may, at any time upon
application, grant permits to shooting galleries, gun clubs and others for
shooting within the City limits in fixed localities and under fixed rules. Such
permits shall be in writing attested by the Clerk-Treasurer conforming to such
requirements as the City Council shall demand, and the permit thus issued shall
be subject to revocation at any time by action of the City Council. (1990 Code
§6-204)
4-3-24: TRESPASSING:
It shall be unlawful for any person to take down any fence or to let down any
bars, or to open any gate in or on the property of another without the consent
of the owner, occupant or person in charge thereof. (1990 Code §6-129)
4-3-25: VAGRANCY:
   A.   Prohibited Acts: Every person without visible means of support, lawful
occupation or employment, who has a physical ability to work, and who does not
seek employment or labor, nor labor when employment is offered him; every
person who shall be found seeking alms as a business or means of support; or
who associates with known thieves or persons of questionable character or
occupation, or who lodges in any other place than is kept for lodging purposes
without the permission of the owner of the property or the person in possession
thereof; every male person who lives in or about houses of ill fame or bawdy
houses, or for any person to habitually consort with common prostitutes,
habitual drunkards, or any user of narcotics, is hereby defined to be a
vagrant.
   B.   Violation A Misdemeanor: Any person who shall be convicted of being a
vagrant shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. (1990 Code §6-131)
CHAPTER 4
MINORS
SECTION:
4-4-1: Curfew
4-4-1: CURFEW:
   A.   Prohibited Hours: It shall be unlawful and a misdemeanor for any minor
(male or female), seventeen (17) years of age or under to be in any public
place or to be upon any street, alley or public grounds within the City between
the hours of ten thirty o'clock (10:30) P.M. and five o'clock (5:00) A.M. on
the nights of Sunday, Monday, Tuesday, Wednesday and Thursday, and between the
hours of twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight and five o'clock (5:00) A.M. on Friday
and Saturday except under the following conditions:
      1.   In attendance at or going to or from a recognized school function.
      2.   In attendance at or going to or from a supervised public, fraternal
or church activity.
      3.   With written permission from a parent or legal guardian for a
specific purpose, and only for a specific date and time. Any blanket permission
shall be considered as being no permission.
      4.   Any proven emergency situation.
      5.   When accompanied by parent(s) or legal guardian.
   B.   Responsibility Of Parents And/Or Guardians: Any parent, parents, legal
guardian or other adult persons having custody or control of any minor or
minors permitting, allowing or abetting said minor or minors to violate
subsection A of this section on a second or subsequent occasion shall be deemed
guilty of a violation of the Youth Rehabilitation Act relating to "encouraging
violations", and the finding that said minor or minors have violated said
section for a second or subsequent time shall be presumptive proof of the
encouraging of a violation of the Youth Rehabilitation Act by said minor or
minors.
   C.   Presumption Of Presence On Street:
      1.   The finding of any minor seventeen (17) years of age or under upon
the streets, alleys or public places within the City during the prohibited
hours without written permission or without a lawfully appearing excuse shall
be prima facie showing of a violation of this section, and upon such showing,
any police officer shall detain said minor or minors for a reasonable time in
order to notify said minor's parent, parents, legal guardian or other adult
having custody or control to pick up said minor or minors at the place of
detention, and a written record, constituting a warning, shall be maintained by
the County Sheriff's Department.
      2.   Upon a second or subsequent violation of this section, minor/minors
and the parent, parents, legal guardian or other person having custody may be
charged with the misdemeanor violation of this section or the laws of the
State. (2018 Code)
CHAPTER 5
ANIMAL CONTROL
SECTION:
4-5-1: Animals And Poultry Running At Large
4-5-2: Tying Livestock
4-5-3: Impounding Animals
4-5-4: Sale Of Impounded Animals
4-5-5: Freeing Impounded Animals Prohibited
4-5-6: Animals On Sidewalks
4-5-7: Cruelty To Animals
4-5-8: Dead Animals
4-5-1: ANIMALS AND POULTRY RUNNING AT LARGE:
   A.   Animals: It shall be unlawful for any person to allow any horse,
cattle, goats, sheep, pigs or hogs or other livestock to run at large in the
City at any time during the year, and it shall be unlawful for anyone to herd
or drive any of the above named animals through the streets without having said
animals under control by means of rope, strap or other device by which they may
be led, unless such animal is being driven in harness or hauled. (1990 Code §6-
501)
   B.   Poultry Or Fowl: It shall be unlawful for any person to keep fowl or
poultry unless such fowl or poultry are at all times kept upon his own premises
and in enclosures. (1990 Code §6-502)
4-5-2: TYING LIVESTOCK:
It shall be unlawful for any person to tie livestock within reach of any
sidewalk or crosswalk or within reach of the fences, buildings, improvements,
trees or shrubbery of any other person within the City or tie livestock to any
telephone or utility pole within the City. (1990 Code §6-503)
4-5-3: IMPOUNDING ANIMALS:
If any animal shall be found running at large contrary to the provisions of
this chapter, it is hereby made the duty of the County Sheriff or Deputy
Sheriff to take and corner the same in a secure place or other place provided
for that purpose and such animal taken up and confined shall not be released
until the owner or person entitled to the possession thereof shall pay to the
officer having such animal in keeping the following: In addition to the cost of
advertising and keeping each animal taken up under this chapter the County
Sheriff or Deputy Sheriff shall collect three dollars ($3.00) for impounding
