the same, said fee to be retained by him for his services and also one dollar
($1.00) for each day he shall have kept the same and ten percent (10%) of the
sales, and the same shall be turned into the Treasury. (1990 Code §6-504; amd.
2018 Code)
4-5-4: SALE OF IMPOUNDED ANIMALS:
   A.   Notice And Sale: If the owner or person entitled to the possession of
an animal within five (5) days from the time it is so taken into custody does
not pay the charges and take it away, it shall be lawful for the County Sheriff
or Deputy Sheriff, having such animal in a cage, to sell at public auction said
animal; having given at least five (5) days' notice of the time and place of
said sale by posting the same in five (5) public places in the City, and a copy
of said notice shall also be served upon the owner or possessor of any said
animal if known, at least five (5) days before the sale, but any such animal
may be redeemed at any time before the sale by the payment to the officer or
his assistant, fees, expenses and charges heretofore provided herein. (1990
Code §6-505; amd. 2018 Code)
   B.   Revenue From Sale: In case any animal sold pursuant to the provisions
of this chapter be sold for more than is sufficient to pay the fees and charges
aforesaid, such excess shall be by the office or his assistant making the sale,
deposited with the Clerk-Treasurer which shall be paid upon an order of the
City Council to the owner of such animal or animals or to the person entitled
to the possession of the same upon claim and proper proof within six (6) months
from the date of said sale. (1990 Code §6-506)
4-5-5: FREEING IMPOUNDED ANIMALS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful to break open or in any manner, directly or indirectly,
aid or assist in breaking open a pen or enclosure with intent of releasing any
animal confined therein pursuant to the provisions of this chapter. (1990 Code
§6-507)
4-5-6: ANIMALS ON SIDEWALKS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to ride, lead or drive any horse, mule,
sheep, pig, goat or cattle upon any sidewalk within the City. (1990 Code §6-
104)
4-5-7: CRUELTY TO ANIMALS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to overdrive, overload, or drive when
overloaded, or overwork, or cruelly beat, mutilate, torture, torment or deprive
of sustenance or abandon, or neglect any animal. (1990 Code §6-106)
4-5-8: DEAD ANIMALS:
It shall be unlawful for the owner of any dead animal in the City to leave the
carcass thereof exposed. (1990 Code §6-113)
ARTICLE A. DOGS
SECTION:
4-5A-1: Purpose
4-5A-2: Definitions
4-5A-3: Licensing Requirements; Fees
4-5A-4: License And Nonlicense Tags; Transfers
4-5A-5: Maximum Number Of Dogs Per Household
4-5A-6: Rabies Quarantine
4-5A-7: Impoundment Of Dogs; Disposition; Fees
4-5A-8: Running At Large Prohibited
4-5A-9: Female Dogs In Heat; Destruction Of Certain Dogs
4-5A-10: Dangerous Dogs; Restrictions; Licensing
4-5A-11: Enforcement; Animal Control Officers
4-5A-12: Interference Prohibited
4-5A-13: Kennel License
4-5A-14: Additional Offenses
4-5A-15: Violations And Remedies Cumulative
4-5A-16: Penalties For Violations
4-5A-17: Liability For Damage To Property
4-5A-18: City Immunity
4-5A-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this article is to provide for regulation of the harboring of
dogs within the City limits, to promote public safety and welfare of the
citizens of the City, and to promote the welfare of dogs harbored within the
City limits. (Ord. 223, 5-5-1997)
4-5A-2: DEFINITIONS:
Unless the context otherwise indicates, the following words and terms used in
this article shall mean:
ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER:
   A.   The Lewis County Sheriff or Deputy; and
   B.   Any other person(s) designated by resolution of the City Council of
Winchester, as an animal control officer as provided in this article.
AT LARGE/RUN AT LARGE: A dog is "at large" or "running at large" if it is off
its harborer's premises and not under control of a person.
BITE: Any closure by an animal's mouth causing a redness, breaking, or tearing
of the skin of any person or which materially damages or destroys the personal
property of another.
DANGEROUS DOG: Any dog declared dangerous as provided in this article.
DOG: Any member, male or female, of the family of Canis Familiaris.
HARBOR/HARBORING: To own or keep a dog within the City limits of the City of
Winchester. It shall be prima facie evidence that a person is harboring a dog
for the purposes of this article if the person: a) is listed as the owner or
harborer of the dog within the City of Winchester on any application for dog
licensing; b) is over eighteen (18) years of age and resides at or is in
physical control of a premises, or part thereof, on which a dog remains or to
which it customarily returns daily for food or shelter for three (3)
consecutive days or more.
HARBORER: Any person who owns a dog or keeps a dog within the City limits of
the City of Winchester.
HARBORER'S PREMISES: All real property under a harborer's ownership, lease, or
control inside the inner line of a sidewalk, or if there is no sidewalk, inside
of the curb, ditch or shoulder marking the edge of the traveled or used portion
of the public right-of-way. Premises also includes the inside of a closed motor
vehicle.
KENNEL: Any premises, other than a veterinary office, animal shelter, grooming
facility, or pet shop, on which three (3) or more dogs are maintained,
harbored, possessed, boarded, bred or cared for.
LEASH: A leash, lead cord, which may not be more than ten feet (10') in length,
by which a dog is physically controlled by the person accompanying it.
NEUTERED DOG: Any male or female dog rendered incapable of reproducing
offspring by surgery or other veterinary medical procedure.
OWNER: Legal owner of a dog.
UNDER CONTROL: A dog is under control if:
   A.   The dog is confined within the boundaries of the harborer's premises;
or
   B.   The dog is not on the harborer's premises but is: 1) confined within a
vehicle; or 2) in the control of a responsible person by use of a leash not
exceeding ten feet (10') in length.
VETERINARY CLINIC OR HOSPITAL: Any establishment maintained and operated by a
licensed veterinarian for the boarding of animals or the diagnosis, treatment,
and care of diseased or injured animals.
(Ord. 223, 5-5-1997)
4-5A-3: LICENSING REQUIREMENTS; FEES:
   A.   License Required; Exceptions:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person to harbor a dog within the City
limits not licensed as provided by this article.
      2.   No license shall be required for dogs which are harbored within the
City limits by the owner thereof if the owner: a) is not a resident of the
City; and b) the dog is harbored less than thirty (30) consecutive days within
the City; and c) the dog is validly licensed by another government licensing
authority.
   B.   Application And Information Required:
      1.   All licenses required under this article shall be issued by the City
Clerk-Treasurer. In addition to payment of all required fees, all applicants
for dog licenses shall provide the following information to the Clerk-Treasurer
as a condition precedent to issuance of a license:
         a.   The name, address and phone number of the owner; and
         b.   The name, address and phone number of the harborer if different
from the owner; and
         c.   The name, age, breed and gender of the dog; and
         d.   An accurate photograph of the dog or a written description of the
weight, size, color and distinguishing characteristics of the dog; and
         e.   Whether the dog has been neutered; and
         f.   Proof of current rabies vaccination; and
         g.   Whether the dog has been declared a dangerous or vicious dog by
any government authority.
      2.   It shall be unlawful for any person to knowingly provide false
information on any application or in applying for any license under this
article.
   C.   Denial Of License:
      1.   Except as may be directed by resolution of the City Council, the
City Clerk-Treasurer shall refuse to issue or renew any license to any person
who:
         a.   Fails to provide any information required to be submitted under
subsection B1 of this section or fails to pay the required license fee; or
         b.   Knowingly provides false information in making application for
any license under this article; or
         c.   Applies for licensing of a dog that has been declared a dangerous
or vicious dog by any governmental authority if disclosed by the applicant or
otherwise made known to the City Clerk-Treasurer. Nothing herein shall require
the Clerk- Treasurer to undertake any independent inquiry of this issue with
any person or governmental authority other than the applicant.
      2.   In the event the City Clerk-Treasurer shall deny the applicant a
license or renewal, the applicant may apply to the City Council for issuance of
a license. The City Council may issue said license by resolution of the Council
on such terms and conditions as the City Council shall deem in the best
interest of the City.
   D.   License Fees:
      1.   The license fees for dogs shall be as follows:
         a.   Neutered dog: Five dollars ($5.00) per year.
         b.   Unneutered dog: Seven dollars ($7.00) per year.
         c.   Replacement tag: Two dollars ($2.00) per year.
         d.   Kennel: One hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) per year.
      2.   No lifetime licenses shall be issued.
   E.   License Term:
      1.   All licenses issued under this article shall expire at twelve
o'clock (12:00) midnight on December 31 of the year in which the license is
issued. A license for the succeeding calendar year may be obtained prior to the
expiration of the current year's license but shall not be effective until the
expiration of the current license. No part of any dog license fee shall be
refundable. (Ord. 223, 5-5-1997)
4-5A-4: LICENSE AND NONLICENSE TAGS; TRANSFERS:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person to allow a dog harbored by the
person to wear any license tag or insignia of licensing other than a valid
license tag issued under this article for the dog wearing the tag. This section
shall not prohibit the wearing of nonlicense tags for the purpose of
identification, proof of vaccination or similar tags if the dog is wearing a
valid current license tag issued under this article for the dog.
   B.   All licenses and tags issued under this article or predecessor
ordinances shall be nontransferable.
   C.   It shall be unlawful for any person to transfer or attempt to transfer
to another person any license or tag issued under this article or predecessor
ordinances. (Ord. 223, 5-5-1997)
4-5A-5: MAXIMUM NUMBER OF DOGS PER HOUSEHOLD:
There shall be no more than two (2) licensed dogs permitted per household or
per harborer, unless the same is qualified and licensed as a kennel. (Ord. 223,
5-5-1997)
4-5A-6: RABIES QUARANTINE:
The animal control officer shall have the authority to order the harborer of
any dog showing symptoms of rabies or any dog which has bitten any person to
subject the dog to the City Pound, veterinarian or any other place in the
business of boarding dogs for quarantine for a period not to exceed fifteen
(15) days, or for such other periods as indicated by a licensed veterinarian as
necessary to determine if the subject dog is infected with rabies. If the dog
is determined to be free of rabies, the dog shall be returned to the harborer
upon payment of one hundred percent (100%) of the regular fee for the keeping
of dogs impounded. If the fee is not paid, the dog shall be subject to disposal
as provided is this article. In lieu of submitting the dog to impoundment, the
harborer may at their expense admit the dog to a licensed veterinarian for
examination and provide the City with a certification that the dog is free from
rabies. Any dog afflicted with rabies shall be disposed of immediately, either
by the harborer or the animal control officer. (Ord. 223, 5-5-1997)
4-5A-7: IMPOUNDMENT OF DOGS; DISPOSITION; FEES:
   A.   Authorization:
      1.   All dogs found running at large within the City limits may be
impounded by the animal control officer by the use of a tranquilizer gun or
other humane means of dog control.
      2.   If a dog is impounded, the animal control officer shall undertake a
reasonable inquiry to determine the identity of the owner or harborer of the
dog. Reasonable inquiry shall consist of and be limited to: a) examining any
tags affixed to any collar worn by the dog at the time of impoundment; and b)
examining the dog licensing records of the City. In the event the identity of
the owner or harborer of the dog is determined from said inquiry, the animal
control officer shall serve the owner or harborer of the dog with written
notice of the impoundment by: a) personal service; or b) regular first class
U.S. mail addressed to the last known mailing address of the owner or harborer
as shown by the records of the City Clerk- Treasurer, with service being
effective on the date of mailing. No such notice shall be required if the
identity of the owner or harborer is not determined from said inquiry.
      3.   The owner or harborer of any dog which may be taken up and impounded
under the provisions of this article may recover possession of the dog upon
payment to the City of any license fees, impoundment fees, and other costs
provided in this article.
   B.   Disposition Of Impounded Dogs: If the owner or harborer of any
impounded dog fails to pay any required fees and costs under this article
within seven (7) days after the date of service of any written notice required
under this section, or within five (5) days of the date of impoundment if no
notice is required, the animal control officer may dispose of the dog:
      1.   By delivering it to any person who will pay all fees and costs due;
or
      2.   By destroying the dog in a humane manner.
   C.   Payment Of Fees And Costs Prior To Release: Impounded dogs shall not be
released until the owner or harborer pays to the City Clerk-Treasurer:
      1.   Ten dollars ($10.00) capture fee; and
      2.   Five dollars ($5.00) per day impoundment fee each day of
impoundment; and
      3.   If the dog has not been issued a valid current City dog license
required under this article, a license fee as provided by this article; and
      4.   Any other reasonable costs and expenses of impoundment incurred by
the City in impounding the dog, including any veterinary expenses reasonably
incurred. (Ord. 223, 5-5-1997)
4-5A-8: RUNNING AT LARGE PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful for any harborer of a dog to permit a harbored dog to:
   A.   Be or run at large; or
   B.   Go or remain upon any public premises not owned by, leased by, or in
the control of the harborer without consent of the owner or occupier of the
private premises. (Ord. 223, 5-5-1997)
4-5A-9: FEMALE DOGS IN HEAT; DESTRUCTION OF CERTAIN DOGS:
All persons harboring any female dog shall keep it shut up when in heat. Any
female dog running at large at such season may be disposed of by the animal
control officer without giving any notice required under section
4-5A-7 of this article or otherwise. The animal control officer may also
dispose of by destroying in a humane manner, any dog found running at large
which, in the judgment of the animal control officer:
   A.   Displays symptoms of contagious disease; or
   B.   Displays serious physical injury or illness and that the animal control
officer deems, in the officer's sole discretion, that it is necessary to
destroy the dog to prevent further suffering; or
   C.   Displays vicious or aggressive behavior which poses imminent risk of
physical injury to any person and the dog cannot, in the discretion of the
animal control officer, be taken into control for impoundment by reasonable
humane methods. (Ord. 223, 5-5-1997)
4-5A-10: DANGEROUS DOGS; RESTRICTIONS; LICENSING:
   A.   Harboring: It shall be unlawful for any person to harbor a dangerous
dog within the City limits except as provided in this article.
   B.   License Issuance Or Renewal: The City Clerk-Treasurer shall not issue
or renew any dog license for any dog that has been declared a dangerous dog by
the City, or dangerous, vicious or other similar classification by any
government authority, except as may be provided by resolution of the City
Council.
   C.   Declaration As Dangerous Dog; Appeal; Hearing:
      1.   The animal control officer may declare a dog to be a dangerous dog
if, upon investigation of any complaint, incident or information otherwise
provided, the animal control officer finds that:
         a.   The dog has, whether or not under control, aggressively bitten
any person, domestic animal or fowl or maliciously damaged or destroyed
property of another; or
         b.   The dog has been declared dangerous, vicious or other similar
declaration by any governmental authority.
      2.   If the animal control officer makes said declaration, the animal
control officer shall notify the owner or harborer of the declaration and the
manner and time limits in which an appeal of the declaration may be taken. Said
notice shall be in writing and served by: a) personal service; or b) regular
first class U.S. mail addressed to the last known mailing address of the owner
or harborer as shown by the records of the City Clerk-Treasurer, with service
being effective on the date of mailing.
      3.   The animal control officer may impound any dog declared to be
dangerous, including, but not limited to, impounding of the dog during the
pendency of any appeal proceeding. The owner and harborer of the dog shall be
liable for all costs and fees of impounding regardless of the final disposition
of the case.
      4.   The owner or harborer of a dog declared dangerous shall have five
(5) business days from the date of service of the written declaration to
request a hearing appealing the declaration. The request for hearing shall be
in writing, identify the name, address and telephone number of the requesting
party, and shall be served upon the City Clerk- Treasurer within the time limit
above provided. In the event no hearing is requested within the time and in the
manner above provided, the animal control officer may dispose of the dog as
provided by subsection 4-5A-7B of this article without further notice to the
owner or harborer.
      5.   If a hearing is requested, a hearing shall be held within seven (7)
days of the date the request for hearing is received by the City Clerk-
Treasurer, or at such other time as is agreed to by the requesting party.
         a.   The Mayor and two (2) City Council members appointed by the Mayor
shall constitute the hearing panel and shall hear the appeal. The hearing shall
be informal and the Idaho Rules of Evidence shall not apply. The owner,
harborer and the animal control officer or other representative of the City
shall be given the opportunity to submit evidence, present witnesses and be
heard on the matter, including the right of cross- examination.
         b.   In determining whether the dog is dangerous, the hearing panel
may consider, among other evidence, past incidents, provocation for the
dangerous behavior, whether the conduct occurred on the premises and any other
fact or allegation relating to the incident from which the declaration arises.
      6.   If the hearing panel shall find that the declaration was proper, the
hearing panel shall either:
         a.   Direct the animal control officer to dispose of the dog as
provided by subsection
4-5A-7B of this article; or
         b.   Direct that the dog may be released to the owner or harborer on
such conditions as the hearing panel shall deem in the best interest of the
City, which may include, but are not limited to: 1) the dog will be removed
from the City limits immediately following release and not be allowed to
return; 2) requiring the owner or harborer to take steps sufficient to confine
the dog in a manner to prevent harm to the public; and 3) requiring the owner
or harborer to provide a surety bond or proof of liability insurance for
compensation of those who may suffer injury by reason of harboring of a
dangerous dog.
      7.   The decision of the hearing panel shall become final unless the
decision is appealed to the District Court within three (3) days following the
date of the decision. (Ord. 223, 5-5-1997)
4-5A-11: ENFORCEMENT; ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICERS:
   A.   The Lewis County law enforcement are hereby appointed and designated as
animal control officers of the City. In addition to all authority granted to
them for general enforcement laws as peace officers, said officers are further
authorized and directed to enforce all portions of this article and perform all
duties of animal control under this article.
   B.   The City Council may appoint such additional persons as it deems
necessary and proper to act as animal control officer(s) who shall be under the
supervision and control of the Mayor. Any such appointment shall be reflected
in the minutes of the City Council or by resolution of the City Council. The
compensation and terms and conditions of contracting or employment of such
person shall be determined from time to time by the City Council.
   C.   All persons designated as animal control officers under this article
may undertake any action or duty as animal control officer provided under this
article concurrently, jointly or individually. (Ord. 223, 5-5-1997)
4-5A-12: INTERFERENCE PROHIBITED:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person to knowingly hinder, molest or
interfere with any animal control officer in the discharge of any of his duties
under this article.
   B.   It shall be unlawful for any person to attempt to remove or remove any
dog or dogs from the City Pound or the possession of the animal control officer
without the consent of the animal control officer or otherwise as provided by
this article. (Ord. 223, 5-5-1997)
4-5A-13: KENNEL LICENSE:
No person shall operate or maintain a kennel within the City without first
obtaining a license therefor. (Ord. 223, 5-5-1997)
4-5A-14: ADDITIONAL OFFENSES:
In addition to other provisions of this article:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person harboring or in control of a dog
to:
      1.   Permit the dog to scatter garbage, refuse or debris; or
      2.   Permit the dog to chase any person, vehicle or domestic animal; or
      3.   Permit the dog to deposit fecal material on any property not that of
its owner or harborer without immediately removing the same from the property;
or
      4.   Permit the dog to bark, howl, or otherwise cause noise in a manner
which unreasonably disturbs, or is likely to disturb, the peace and quiet of
any person; or
      5.   Harbor one or more dogs in such a manner that the keeping of the dog
results in nauseous, foul or offensive odor or so as to create a public
nuisance; or
      6.   Harbor a dog and fail to provide the dog with food, water, shelter
or necessary veterinary care, which shall include a rabies vaccination every
three (3) years.
   B.   It shall be unlawful for any person to beat, abuse or otherwise engage
in cruel or inhumane treatment of a dog. (Ord. 223, 5-5-1997)
4-5A-15: VIOLATIONS AND REMEDIES CUMULATIVE:
The violations, punishments and remedies provided in this article shall be
cumulative with other provisions of this Code, State and Federal laws, and the
City may cause any conduct or condition in violation of this article
constituting a public nuisance to be abated as a public nuisance in the manner
provided by law. (Ord. 223, 5-5-1997)
4-5A-16: PENALTIES FOR VIOLATIONS:
In addition to other penalties and remedies provided by this article, any
person violating any provision of this article shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor. The following minimum sentences shall be imposed as follows in all
cases:
   A.   Upon conviction for a first offense, a minimum fine of twenty five
dollars ($25.00) plus court costs shall be assessed.
   B.   Upon conviction for a second offense, a minimum of seventy five dollars
($75.00) plus court costs shall be assessed.
   C.   Upon conviction for a third or subsequent offense, a minimum fine of
three hundred dollars ($300.00) plus court costs shall be assessed.
   D.   Upon conviction for a fourth offense involving the same animal and/or
the same owner, the animal shall be destroyed in a humane manner by the animal
control officer. (Ord. 223, 5-5-1997)
4-5A-17: LIABILITY FOR DAMAGE TO PROPERTY:
The owner or harborer of any dog that does damage to property of another shall
be liable to the owner of the property damaged for the damages and costs of
suit. In the prosecution of actions for such damages, it is not necessary for
the plaintiff to show that the owner or harborer of such dog has knowledge of
the fact that such dog was doing damage to the property. (Ord. 223, 5-5-1997)
4-5A-18: CITY IMMUNITY:
The City, its officials, employees, animal control officers and agents shall
not be liable for any acts or omissions in performing duties arising from this
article and shall be immune from suit on any claims arising by reason of any
such alleged act or omission. (Ord. 223, 5-5-1997)
CHAPTER 6
DISCRIMINATION IN HOUSING
SECTION:
4-6-1: City Policy
4-6-2: Enforcement
4-6-3: Affirmative Action Program
4-6-1: CITY POLICY:
The City does hereby adopt, for the purpose of providing for equal housing
within the City, a prohibition against discrimination in housing on the basis
of race, color, religion, sex, disability or national origin. Such
discrimination may not occur in the sale, rental, lease, financing of homes or
land to be used for the construction of homes or lands or in the provision of
brokerage services within the City.
(1990 Code §4-405; amd. 2018 Code)
4-6-2: ENFORCEMENT:
The City of Winchester, being a small City and having no means of investigating
or conciliating complaints filed alleging discrimination in housing will,
therefore, assist all persons who feel they have been discriminated against
because of race, color, religion, sex, disability or national origin to seek
equity under the law, by filing a complaint through the City with the Idaho
Human Rights Commission or the U.S. Department of Housing and Urban
Development, Seattle Regional Office Compliance Division.
(1990 Code §4-406; amd. 2018 Code)
4-6-3: AFFIRMATIVE ACTION PROGRAM:
   A.   The City will become actively involved in any Voluntary Affirmative
Marketing Agreement as entered into by any local or State Board of Realtors and
the Department of Housing and Urban Development.
   B.   But, the City will take efforts as are appropriate to the community to
establish a Voluntary Areawide Equal Opportunity Plan between the City and the
Department of Housing and Urban Development.
   C.   The City will create a fair housing program for owners, tenants,
lenders, prospective buyers and developers or builders to educate them as to
respective rights under the law concerning title VIII of the Civil Rights Act
of 1968 as well as any local and State Fair Housing Laws, ordinances and
resolutions.
   D.   This program will include, but not be limited to, the printing of and
publicizing of this chapter and other information through local media such as
newspapers and radio stations; also distributing posters and fliers and any
other means which will bring to the attention of those affected, the knowledge
of their respective rights concerning equal opportunity. (1990 Code §4-407)
TITLE 5
TRAFFIC, PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND PUBLIC WAYS
SECTION:
5-1-1: Excavations
5-1-2: Snow And Ice Removal
5-1-3: Trees And Shrubbery
5-1-4: Sidewalk Construction And Repair
5-1-1: EXCAVATIONS:
   A.   Open Excavations: No landowner or tenant shall permit an excavation for
a basement, or other excavation hazardous to human life, to remain open on land
owned or occupied by any person, firm or corporation without covering the same
securely to prevent injuries to persons; provided, however, that the same may
remain open during the course of construction or for the purpose of cleaning
the same. (1990 Code §4-101)
   B.   Warning Signs Required: No excavation hazardous to human life shall be
permitted to remain open unless the same is properly safeguarded at all times
by barricades and warning signs. (1990 Code §4-102)
   C.   Abandoned Excavations: All excavations, hazardous to human life, which
are no longer in use or have been abandoned shall be filled with earth to the
level of the surrounding ground. An excavation for the basement of a building
shall be deemed to have been abandoned when construction has stopped for a
period of thirty (30) days. (1990 Code §4-103)
   D.   Hazardous Excavations: Any excavation shall be determined to be prima
facie hazardous to human life if its depth exceeds two feet (2'). (1990 Code
§4-104)
5-1-2: SNOW AND ICE REMOVAL:
   A.   Removal Required: The owner, tenant or occupant of any premises within
the City abutting or adjoining any public sidewalk shall remove all snow and
ice from any such sidewalk. (1990 Code §9-101)
   B.   Giving Notice: It shall be the duty of the City to notify any owner,
tenant or occupant of property herein described to remove or otherwise correct
the objectionable matter herein legislated against, which notice shall be sent
by registered mail to the last known address of such owner, tenant or occupant,
notifying him that he has a period of twenty four (24) hours from and after
receipt of such notice, within which to correct or otherwise remove the
objections set forth in said notice. (1990 Code §9-102)
   C.   Failure To Comply; City Removal: Upon failure of the owner, tenant or
occupant of said premises to comply with the terms and conditions of said
notice, then and in that event the City shall have the right to remove such
snow and ice and assess the cost thereof against the premises abutting the
sidewalk. Such assessment shall be certified to the County Assessor or other
proper County officials having charge of the making of the assessment roll, and
such assessment shall be placed on the assessment roll and collected in the
same manner as other City Taxes are collected. (1990 Code §9-103)
5-1-3: TREES AND SHRUBBERY:
   A.   Trimming Trees: Any owner or occupant of any real property shall trim
all trees on property owned or occupied by him, overhanging the sidewalks,
streets or alleys, so that the branches thereon will not interfere with
pedestrians or public travel. (1990 Code §9-201)
   B.   Hedges And Shrubbery: Any owner or occupant of any real property shall
trim all hedges and shrubbery adjacent to public sidewalks so that no part of
said hedges and/or shrubbery shall extend over any part of a public sidewalk in
the City. (1990 Code §9-202)
   C.   Injury To Trees Or Shrubbery: It is hereby declared unlawful for any
person, not the owner thereof, or without lawful authority to do so, to
wilfully injure, deface, disfigure or destroy any fruit, and/or ornamental tree
or shrub, or to injure, destroy, cut or pick any flower or plant growing,
standing, or being either on private ground or any street, parking, public park
or place within the City. (1990 Code §9-203)
   D.   Trees Outside Property Line: The City Council is hereby given full and
complete control over all trees growing within the confines of the limits of
the City which are outside the property lines of the respective lots, plots and
tracts. (1990 Code §9-204)
5-1-4: SIDEWALK CONSTRUCTION AND REPAIR:
   A.   Inspection; Council Determination: The City Council shall designate one
of its members whose duty it shall be to inspect all sidewalks within the City
and report to the Council, where in his judgment the construction of a new
sidewalk is necessary, and all cases where there is no existing sidewalk, and
in his judgment it is necessary for a sidewalk to be constructed. After
considering such report and recommendation, the Council shall make its
determination. Said member shall report such fact to the Council with his
recommendation. Whenever the Council, after considering such report and
recommendation, in their judgment deem it necessary to require property owners
within the City to construct or repair sidewalks, they shall take recorded
action in an official City Council meeting, naming the owner and location of
property abutting it which it is in such meeting determined sidewalks shall be
constructed and repaired. (1990 Code §9-301)
   B.   Notice To Construct: When any sidewalk is ordered to be constructed or
reconstructed, under the provisions of this section, the Clerk-Treasurer, as
soon as may be, shall serve notice in writing upon the property owner, or any
resident agent of the property owner, directing such sidewalk to be constructed
or reconstructed, of the materials and according to the specifications in force
in the district where such is to be constructed or reconstructed, and
describing the premises adjacent to which such construction is to be made. The
service of such notice may be made by delivery of a copy thereof to the owner
or his agent, or if neither is to be found within the City by mailing a copy
thereof to the owner at his last known post office address, and service by mail
shall be deemed complete upon the expiration of five (5) days from the date of
the mailing of such notice. (1990 Code §9-302)
   C.   Failure To Construct: If the work of building such sidewalk in
accordance with the notice served by the Clerk-Treasurer is not begun within
ten (10) days after the serving of such notice, or if after having been begun,
the same is not completed within a reasonable time thereafter, the Mayor and
the Council shall notify the City Clerk-Treasurer of such fact and the Clerk-
Treasurer shall call for bids by publication for two (2) consecutive issues in
some newspaper published in or having a general circulation in the City for the
construction and completion of such sidewalk. Such bids shall be returned by
the Clerk-Treasurer to the Mayor and opened and considered at the next or any
general or special meeting; and after laying over not less than one day, the
contract for the construction or completion of such sidewalk shall be let to
the lowest and best reasonable bidder, and the work of construction or
reconstruction shall be performed under the general supervision of the Public
Works Director. (1990 Code §9-303)
   D.   Repairs: When any sidewalk within the City is in such condition as in
the judgment of the City Council to require repairs thereof to be made, the
Clerk-Treasurer shall serve upon the owner or his agent a written notice to
make such repairs, describing the same in general terms, which notice may
require the repairs to be made within such reasonable time, not exceeding ten
(10) days after the service of such notice as may, in the opinion of the
Council, be deemed necessary, and if such repairs be not made within the time
required by such notice, the same shall thereupon be made by the Public Works
Director. (1990 Code §9-304)
   E.   Serving Of Itemized Statement; Collection: Upon the completion of the
construction or repairs, the costs thereof shall be paid out of any
unappropriated monies in the General Fund of the City or such other fund as may
be designated by the City Council. As soon as may be thereafter, the Clerk-
Treasurer shall serve upon the owner of such property, or his agent, in the
same manner as the notice to construct sidewalks is authorized to be served, an
itemized statement of the costs of such construction, reconstruction or repair,
and if the costs thereof be not paid within five (5) days after such service,
the Clerk-Treasurer shall deliver a copy of such itemized statement to the City
Attorney who shall proceed to collect the same. (1990 Code §9-305)
   F.   Duties Of City Attorney; Lien: Upon the receiving of any such
statement, the City Attorney shall, as soon as may be, bring suit in any court
having jurisdiction, for the recovery of the monies expended by the City in the
construction, reconstruction or repair of such sidewalk, or shall file a lien
upon the property abutting upon such sidewalk. Such lien shall be verified and
shall be filed and foreclosed as in the case of other liens under the general
laws of the State of Idaho and amendments which may hereafter be made thereto,
and from the date of the filing of the same, the costs of such construction,
maintenance and repairs shall be and remain a lien upon the property described
as in the case of other liens. (1990 Code §9-306; amd. 2018 Code)
   G.   Hearing On Notice To Construct: Any time after the service of the
notice to construct, reconstruct or repair, as hereinbefore provided, and
before the expiration of the time specified therein, the owner or agent upon
whom such service was made may appear before the City Council at any general or
special meeting and show cause why the order for such construction,
reconstruction, or repair should be revoked. The City shall hear and determine
such application informally and such application shall not extend the period
within which the work is to be begun unless otherwise ordered by the City
Council. (1990 Code §9-307)
CHAPTER 2
BILL POSTING AND HANDBILLS
SECTION:
5-2-1: Littering Public Thoroughfares
5-2-2: Posting On Fences, Walls Or Poles
5-2-3: Penalty
5-2-1: LITTERING PUBLIC THOROUGHFARES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to scatter or throw upon the streets,
sidewalks, alleys or other public thoroughfares of the City, any handbills,
posters, advertisements or papers. Nothing herein shall be construed to
authorize any person to obstruct the public streets, sidewalks, alleys or
thoroughfares of the City or create any nuisance therein. The provisions of
this chapter shall not interfere or prevent the posting of notices required by
law to be posted. (1990 Code §5-601)
5-2-2: POSTING ON FENCES, WALLS OR POLES:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person to post, paint, tack or otherwise
attach any notice or other advertising matter to any fence, wall or building or
other property until first obtaining the consent of the owner of such property.
   B.   It shall be unlawful for any person to post, paint, tack or otherwise
attach any notice or advertising matter to any telephone, electric or other
such poles. (1990 Code §5-602)
5-2-3: PENALTY:
Any person violating the provisions of this chapter shall, upon conviction
thereof, be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished pursuant to
section
1-4-1 of this Code. (1990 Code §5-603)
CHAPTER 3
TRAFFIC
SECTION:
5-3-1: Definitions

5-3-8: When Lewis County Sheriff Or Deputies Remove Parked Cars: Costs
5-3-9: Removal Of Unidentified, Stolen, Wrecked Or Abandoned Motor Vehicles And
Charges Therefor
5-3-10: Enforcement Of County's Lien On Properties Impounded By Lewis County
Sheriff’s Department
5-3-11: Proof Of Ownership; Appeal; Redemption After Sale
5-3-12: Penalty

section:
ALLEY:        That thoroughfare which intersects blocks at the rear of the lots of said blocks
              or transverses between regularly established streets.
AUTHORIZED    Vehicles of the Fire Department (Fire Patrol), police vehicles, and such
EMERGENCY     ambulances and emergency vehicles of the municipal departments or public service
VEHICLE:      corporations as the designated or authorized by the City Council.
BICYCLE:      Every device propelled by human power upon which any person may ride, having two

BUSINESS      industrial purposes, including but not limited to hotels, banks or office
DISTRICT:     buildings, railroad stations and public buildings which occupy at least three
              hundred (300) feet of frontage on one side or three hundred (300) feet
              collectively on both sides in use for business.
COMMERCIAL    Every vehicle designed, maintained or used primarily for the transportation of
VEHICLE:      property.

ACCESS        abutting property or lands and other persons have no legal right or access to or

              the lateral lines of the sidewalk on opposite sides of the highway measured from

              indicated for pedestrian crossing by lines or other markings on the surface.
CURB LOADING  A space adjacent to a curb reserved for the exclusive use of vehicles during the
ZONE:         loading or unloading of passengers for materials.
DRIVER:       Every person who drives or in actual physical control of a vehicle.
FREIGHT CURB  A space adjacent to a curb for the exclusive use of vehicles during the loading
LOADING ZONE: or unloading of freight.
              The area embraced within the prolongation or connection of the lateral curb
              lines, or, if none, then the lateral boundary lines of the roadways of the two
INTERSECTION: highways which join one another at or approximately at right angles, or the area
              which within vehicles traveling upon different highways joining at any other
              angle may come in conflict.
LANED         A roadway which is divided into two or more clearly marked lanes for vehicular
ROADWAY:      traffic.

              Every motor vehicle having a saddle for the use of the rider and designed to
MOTORCYCLE:   travel on not more than three wheels in contact with the ground, but excluding a
              tractor.
OFFICIAL TIME Whenever certain hours are named herein, they shall mean Pacific Standard Time.
STANDARD:

TRAFFIC-      placed or erected by authority of a public body or official having jurisdiction,
CONTROL       for the purpose of regulating, warning or guiding traffic.
DEVICES:
              When prohibited means the standing of a vehicle whether occupied or not,
PARK:         otherwise than temporarily for the purpose of and while actually engaged in
              loading or unloading.
PEDESTRIAN:   Any person afoot.

OFFICER:      or regulate traffic or to make arrest for violation of traffic regulations.

OR DRIVEWAY:  owner and those having express or implied permission from the owner, but not by
              other persons.
              The territory contiguous to and including a highway not comprising a business
RESIDENCE     district when the property on such highway for a distance of three hundred (300)
DISTRICT:     feet or more is in the main improved with residence or residences and buildings
              in use for business.

              That portion of a street or highway improved, designed or ordinarily used for
ROADWAY:      vehicular travel, exclusive of the berm or shoulder. In the event a highway
              includes two or more separate roadways the term "roadway" as used herein shall

STOP:         When required means complete cessation of movement.
STOP,         When prohibited means any stopping or standing of a vehicle whether occupied or
STOPPING OR   not, except when necessary to avoid conflict with other traffic or in compliance
STANDING:     with the directions of a police officer or traffic-control sign or signal.

HIGHWAY:      any part thereof is open to the use of the public for the purpose of vehicular

THROUGH       traffic from intersecting streets or highways is required by law to stop before
HIGHWAY:      entering or crossing the same and when stop signs are erected as provided in this
              act.
TRAFFIC:      Pedestrians, ridden or herded animals, vehicles and other conveyances whether
              singly or together while using any public thoroughfare for the purpose of travel.
              Every devise in, upon or by which any person or property is or may be transported
VEHICLES:     or drawn upon a highway, except devises moved by human power or used exclusively
              upon stationary tracks or rails.
 
5-3-2: ANGLE PARKING:
The commissioner or Public Protection is hereby authorized to determine, from
time to time, which streets are of sufficient width to permit angle parking and
after determination that such parking is in the best interests of orderly
movement of traffic, of optimum use of available parking space and of public
safety may be written authorization, filed with the City Clerk, designate such
areas as angle parking only.
"Angle Parking" as used herein shall mean that any vehicle parked within such
an area shall be parked with the right front wheel of said vehicle against the
curb, or as near thereto as practical, with the angle formed between the
longitudinal axis of the vehicle and the curb line so the right-hand side of
the vehicle not more than 70 degrees nor less than 50 degrees. Within such
areas designated for angle parking, no other manner of parking shall be
permitted.
No vehicle or combination of vehicles with a maximum overall length of more
than twenty (20) feet shall be parked in an area designated for angle parking.
Any area designated for angle parking shall be signed as required by Section
5-3-6 of the Revised and Compiled Ordinances of the City of Winchester, and
applicable laws of the State of Idaho.
This section shall not relieve any person from the duty to observe other and
more restrictive provisions prohibiting or limiting the stopping, standing or
parking of vehicles in specified places or at specified times.
5-3-3: PARKING CITATIONS:
Pursuant to Idaho Code 50-3-15A and Rule 14(c)(1) OF THE Idaho Supreme Court
Rules of Procedure in Traffic Cases, the following procedure is hereby adopted
to ensure efficient disposition and enforcement of laws, ordinances and
regulations governing the parking of vehicles within the city.
In lieu of citing a violator of vehicle parking regulations in District Court,
any Lewis County sheriff or his deputies may issue a citation in the form
hereinafter provided.
Any person accused of a violation of an ordinance prohibiting parking a vehicle
in a designated area or restricting the length of time a vehicle may be there
parked, may settle and compromise the claim against him or her for such illegal
parking by paying to the city a bond in the sum of five dollars ($5.00) within
five (5) days of the time such citation was issued. Any Lewis county sheriff or
his deputies is hereby authorized to refrain from instituting prosecution for
the alleged offense involved so long as compliance is had with the procedures
herein.
The citation used for parking violations shall consist of at least two parts,
assembled so the entries on the citation shall reproduce on the other part of
the parts by carbon paper or other means. Each of the parts shall contain, as a
minimum, space to write the date, time and location of violation, the violation
by a brief description, the ordinance or statute number, the vehicle
description, the registration, plate number and state, the Lewis County Sheriff
or his deputies' signature and the last permissible day for posting bond. In
addition, the citation shall be serially numbered and shall contain a
certification that the Lewis County Sheriff or his deputy has reasonable
grounds to believe the offense was committed and contain a notice to the
violator that a complaint can be filed in the District Court in the event of
noncompliance.
This section shall not apply to persons parking a vehicle so as to obstruct the
entrance or exit of any place where police or fire apparatus or other emergency
equipment is kept or housed. Nor shall this section apply to any person charged
with parking in such a way as to reduce traffic on an arterial street to one-
way traffic only; nor to any person whose parking creates an immediate
hazardous traffic situation, nor to any person who refuses to move an illegally
parked vehicle at the request of any Lewis County Sheriff or his deputies.
In all cases where a citation has been issued pursuant to this section, the
issuing Sheriff or deputy shall cause a formal complaint to be filed in the
District Court pursuant to state law and court rules when:
   A.   The violator has failed to post bond, or
   B.   The violator makes a request of Lewis County Sheriff or his deputies
that the matter be so handled, which request must be made within five (5)
working days of the violation and before bond has been posted.
All moneys paid by a violator pursuant to the section shall be paid to the
District Court.
5-3-4: SNOWMOBILES:
The term "snowmobile" shall mean every self-propelled devise upon a combination
of skis, skids, tracks or endless belts, in and upon or by which any person or
property is or may be transported or drawn upon snow- or snow-covered surface
areas, expressly includes devises knows as "snowmobiles" or "ski mobiles".
It shall be lawful to operate a snowmobile upon all the public roadways of the
City of Winchester upon the condition and subject to the restrictions
hereinafter set forth in this section.
No person under the age of fourteen (14) years shall drive or operate a
snowmobile in the City.
It shall be unlawful to for any person to knowingly permit, allow or encourage
the operation or driving of a snowmobile by a person under the age of fourteen
(14) years.
No snowmobile shall be operated in the city, unless it is equipped with the
following:
   A.   At least one and not more than two (2) head lamps sufficient to render
clearly discernible persons and vehicles at a distance of two hundred fifty
(250') feet ahead.
   B.   Tail lamps, which when lighted shall emit a red light plainly visible
at a distance of two hundred fifty feet (250') to the rear.
   C.   At least one brake which may be operated by hand or foot.
   D.   A muffler in good working order and in constant operation to prevent
excessive or unusual noise and annoying smoke; and no person shall us a muffler
cut out, by-pass or similar device.
   E.   All snowmobiles operated in the City shall be equipped with a mast or
antenna displaying area or red-orange, fluorescent flag or pennant a minimum of
five feet (5') above the ground; such flag or pennant shall be either
rectangular or triangular in shape with the leading edge being a minimum 0f six
inches (6') and the length a minimum of twelve inches (12").
Regulations for Operation of Snowmobiles:
   A.   It shall be unlawful to drive, operate or park a snowmobile on any
sidewalk in the City.
   B.   No snowmobile shall be operated at a speed in excess of fifteen (15)
miles per hour in the City.
   C.   No snowmobile shall carry passengers or weights in excess of the
capacity recommended by the manufacture thereof.
   D.   No sled, toboggan, trailer or any other device shall be towed by a
snowmobile except by means of a rigid tow bar connecting the same to such
device.
   E.   No person on skis shall be towed behind a snowmobile.
   F.   It shall be unlawful to drive or operate a snowmobile while under the
influence of intoxicating liquor.
   G.   All snowmobiles shall come to a full stop at all street intersections.
   H.   All snowmobiles shall be operated only in the single file on the
extreme right-hand side of the street.
   I.   Operation of snowmobiles on the streets of the City shall be limited to
ingress and egress to and from the City; that City streets are not to be used
as a place of recreation for snowmobiles.
   J.   No snowmobiles shall be operated within the City limits after ten
o’clock (10:00) P.M. except for the purpose of going directly to or from the
place of residence of the operator of such snowmobile or to its place of
storage.
   K.   No person shall operate a snowmobile carelessly and heedlessly, or
without due caution and circumspection and at a speed or in a manner as to
endanger or be likely to endanger any person or property.
If any provision, section, part of section, sentence or clause of this section
shall be held unconstitutional or invalid, all other parts or provisions not
expressly held to be so void or unconstitutional shall continue in full force
and effect.
Any person convicted of a violation of this section shall be punished by a fine
not to exceed three hundred dollars ($300.00) or imprisonment in the County
jail not more than thirty (30) days or by both such fine and imprisonment.
5-3-5: STOPPING, STANDING OR PARKING PROHIBITED IN SPECIFIED PLACES:
   A.   Stopping, Standing or Parking Prohibited; No Signs required: No person
shall stop, stand or park a vehicle, except when necessary to avoid conflict
with other traffic or in compliance with law or the direction of a Lewis County
Sheriff or his deputies or traffic-control device, in any of the following
places:
      1.   On a sidewalk;
      2.   In front of a public or private driveway;
      3.   Within an intersection;
      4.   Within fifteen (15) feet of a fire hydrant;
      5.   On a cross walk.
      6.   Within twenty (20) feet of a cross walk at an intersection;
      7.   Within thirty (30) feet upon the approach of any flashing beacon,
stop sign, or traffic control device located at the side of the roadway;
      8.   Between a safety zone and adjacent curb or within thirty (30) feet
of points on the curb immediately opposite the ends of a safety zone, unless
the Traffic Division has indicated a different length by signs or markings;
      9.   Within twenty (20) feet of the driveway entrance to any fire station
and on the side of a street opposite the entrance to any fire station and on
the side of the street opposite the entrance to any fire station within
seventy-five (75) feet of said entrance when properly sign-posted;
      10.   Alongside or opposite any street obstruction or excavation when
stopping, standing or parking would obstruct traffic;
      11.   On a roadway side of any vehicle stopped or parked at the edge or
curb of a street;
      12.   Within a highway tunnel; and
      13.   At any place where official signs prohibit stopping.
   B.   No person shall move a vehicle not lawfully under his control into any
such prohibited area or away from a curb such distance as is lawful.
   C.   Parking Not to Obstruct Traffic: No person shall park any vehicle upon
a street, other than an alley, in such a manner or under such conditions as to
leave available less than ten (10) feet of the width of the roadway for free
movement of vehicular traffic.
   D.   Parking in Alleys: No person shall park a vehicle within an alley in
such a manner or under such conditions as to leave available less than ten (10)
feet of the width of the roadway for the free movement of vehicular traffic,
and no person shall stop, stand or park within an alley in such position as to
block the driveway entrance to any abutting property.
   E.   Parking for Certain Purposed Prohibited: No person shall park a vehicle
upon any roadway for the principal purpose of:
      1.   Displaying such a vehicle for sale.
      2.   Washing, greasing or repairing such vehicle except repairs
necessitated by an emergency.
   F.   Parking Adjacent to Schools:
      1.   The traffic division is hereby authorized to erect signs including
no parking upon either or both sides of any street adjacent to any school
property when such parking would, in its opinion, interfere with traffic or
create a hazardous situation.
      2.   When official signs are erected indicated no parking upon either
side of a street adjacent to any school property as authorized herein, no
person shall park a vehicle in any such designated place.
   G.   Parking Prohibited on Narrow Streets:
      1.   The traffic division is hereby authorized to erect signs indicating
no parking upon any street when the width of the roadway does not exceed twenty
(20) feet, or upon one side of a street as indicated by such signs when the
width of the roadway does not exceed thirty (30) feet.
      2.   When official signs prohibiting parking are erected upon narrow
streets as authorized herein, no person shall park a vehicle upon any such
street in violation of any such sign.
   H.   No Stopping, Standing or Parking Near Hazardous or Congested Places:
      1.   The Traffic Division is hereby authorized to determine and designate
by proper signs places not exceeding 100 feet in length in which the stopping,
standing or parking of vehicles would create an especially hazardous condition
or would cause unusual delay to traffic.
      2.   When official signs are erected at hazardous or congested places as
authorized herein no person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle in any such
designation place.
5-3-6: STOPPING FOR LOADING OR UNLOADING ONLY:
   A.   Mayor and City Council to designate Curb Loading Zones: The Mayor and
City Council is hereby authorized to determine the location of passenger and
freight curb loading zones and shall place and maintain appropriate signs
indicating the same and stating the hours during which the provisions of this
section are applicable.
   B.   Standing in Freight Curb Loading Zone: No person shall stop, stand or
park a vehicle for any purpose or length of time other than for the expeditious
unloading and delivery or pick-up and loading of materials in any place marked
as freight curb loading zone hours when the provisions applicable to such zones
are in effect. In no case shall the stop for loading and unloading of materials
exceed thirty (30) minutes.
   C.   Mayor and City Council to Designate Public Carrier Stop and Stands: The
Mayor and City Council is hereby authorized and required to establish bus
stops, and bus stands, and stand for other passenger common-carrier motor
vehicles on such public streets in such places and in such number it shall
determine to be of the greatest benefit and convenience to the public, and
every such bus stop, bus stand, or other stand shall be designated by
appropriate signs.
   D.   Stopping, Standing and Parking of Buses and Regulations:
      1.   The operator of a bus shall not stand or park such vehicle upon any
street at any place other than at a bus stand so designated.
      2.   The operator of a bus shall not stop such vehicle upon any street at
any place for the purpose of loading or unloading passengers or their baggage
other than at a bus stop, bus stand, or passenger loading zone so designated,
except in case of emergency.
      3.   The operator of a buss shall enter a bus stop, bus stand, or
passenger loading zone on a public street in such a manner that the bus when
stopped to load or unload passenger or baggage shall be in a position with the
right front wheel of such vehicle not farther than 18 inches from the curb and
the bus approximately parallel to the curb, so as not to unduly impede the
movement of other vehicle traffic.
   E.   Restricted Use of Bus Stands: No person shall stop, stand or park a
vehicle other than a bus in a bus stop, except that the driver of a passenger
vehicle may temporarily stop therein for the purpose of and while actually
engaged in loading passengers when such stopping does not interfere with any
bus waiting to enter or about to enter such zone.
5-3-7: STOPPING, STANDING OR PARKING RESTRICTED OR PROHIBITED ON CERTAIN
STREETS:
   A.   Application of Section: The provisions of this section prohibiting the
standing or parking of a vehicle shall apply at all times or at those times
herein specified or as indicated on official signs except when it is necessary
to stop a vehicle to avoid conflict with other traffic or in compliance with
the directions of a police officer or official traffic-control devices.
   B.   Regulations Not Exclusive: The provisions of tis section imposing a
time limit on parking shall not relieve any person from the city to observe
other and more restrictive provisions prohibiting or limiting the stopping,
standing or parking of vehicles in specified places or at specified times.
   C.   Parking Signs Required: Whenever by this Chapter any parking time limit
is imposed, it shall be the duty of the Traffic Division to erect appropriate
signs giving notice thereof, and no such regulations shall be effective unless
said signs are erected and in place at the time of any alleged offense.
5-3-8: WHEN LEWIS COUNTY SHERIFF OR DEPUTIES REMOVE PARKED CARS: COSTS:
If at any time a vehicle is parked in a prohibited place or at a time when
parking is prohibited where parked, for a period of ten minutes or more and
such vehicle is obstructing the free movement of traffic or is causing a
traffic hazard, or is directly interfering with the maintenance or care, or
emergency use of the streets, and the person in charge cannot be immediately
located, of if located, fails, neglects or refuses to move said vehicle at
once, the Lewis County Sheriff's Department may in its discretion in addition
to the penalty provided therefore remove or cause to be removed, said vehicle
keeping it in its custody or until the owner or his authorized agent applies
for same and has paid a reasonable cost for removing and storing said vehicle
which costs shall be assessed and collected by the Lewis County Sheriff's Dept.
and said costs and expenses shall be a lien in favor of the Lewis County
Sheriff's Department on said care, provided that when any such motor vehicle is
interfering with the maintenance or emergency use of the streets, but not
otherwise violating this Chapter then the Lewis County Sheriff's Department
may, in its own discretion remove said motor vehicle or other vehicle and care
for the same, and may in its own discretion deliver the same to the owner
without any cost or charge for such removal or storage.
5-3-9: REMOVAL OF UNIDENTIFIED, STOLEN, WRECKED OR ABANDONED MOTOR VEHICLES AND
CHARGES THEREFOR:
The Lewis County Sheriff's Department is hereby authorized in its discretion,
in addition to any penalty that may be provided therefore, to remove an
unidentified, stolen, wrecked or abandoned motor vehicle or other personal
property, as herein defined, found upon any public street or property and shall
keep the same in its custody and control at such place as may be designated by
said Lewis County sheriff Department until redeemed by the owner thereof, as
herein provided; and as such unidentified, stolen, wrecked or abandoned motor
vehicles or other personal property which now is in its possession shall be
subject to the actual cost of removal or tow-in from the public place, and a
storage charge of fifty cents ($0.50) per day as long as the same in is
possession and custody of said department.
 
                                        An automobile or personal property
                                        which remains upon the streets or other
ABANDONED MOTOR VEHICLE OR OTHER        public property for a period longer
PERSONAL PROPERTY:                      than forty-eight (48) hours, the owner
                                        of which cannot be located, or the
                                        owner refused to remove the same.
STOLEN MOTOR VEHICLE OR OTHER PERSONAL  That property which the Lewis County

                                        grounds to believe to be stolen.
UNIDENTIFIED MOTOR VEHICLE OR OTHER     Such motor vehicle or other personal

                                        place unattended.
 
It shall be unlawful for any owner or any person in charge of a motor vehicle
or other personal property, to leave or abandon the same upon the streets or
public places as in this Chapter provided.
5-3-10: ENFORCEMENT OF COUNTY'S LIEN ON PROPERTIES IMPOUNDED BY LEWIS COUNTY
SHERIFF'S DEPARTMENT:
All motor vehicles and other personal property impounded or heretofore
impounded by the Lewis County Sheriff's Department and un-redeemed by the owner
t hereof for a period of forty-five (45) days shall thereafter be subject to
sale to the highest bidder for cash as hereinafter provided, and the proceeds
of said sale shall be deposited with the Treasurer and the balance of said sum,
if any, shall be deposited with the Treasurer and shall be kept in a separate
fund for a period of one year from the date of receipt, and if at the end of
said year the former owner of said property has not made satisfactory proof of
claim as hereinafter provided, then the balance of said proceeds of sale shall
be credited to the General Fund.
5-3-11: PROOF OF OWNERSHIP; APPEAL; REDEMPTION AFTER SALE:
Any person claiming to be the owner of any impounded property as in this
Chapter provided, shall make written application therefor to the Lewis County
Sheriff Department and shall furnish to said Department such additional proof
as may be required to establish said ownership. If he shall present to said
Department said proof of his ownership of said impounded property prior to the
date of actual sale thereof pursuant to the provisions of this Chapter, then
the property itself delivered to said owner under the conditions herein
provided; but if said property has been sold, then said department shall
endorse its findings of ownership with a copy of the written application
addressed to the Clerk, and said owner may present said application and
findings to said Clerk, and if presented within one year after said sale, then
such balance of the proceeds of sale, after deductions as in this Chapter
provided, shall be paid to said owner.
Any appeal from the removal, storage and publications costs, if any, assessed
by the Lewis County Sheriff's Department as provided in this chapter shall be
in the same manner as provided by law.
5-3-12: PENALTY:
Any person violating any of the provisions of this Chapter shall, upon
conviction thereof, be liable to a fine of not more than three hundred dollars
($300) for any one offense, or six (6) months in jail or both, and all such
fines shall be recoverable by said City with cost.
CHAPTER 4
RECREATIONAL VEHICLE GUIDELINES
SECTION:
5-4-1: Purpose
5-4-2: Definitions
5-4-3: Application And Permits
5-4-4: Requirement For Recreational Vehicle Parks
5-4-1: PURPOSE:
The City Council of the City of Winchester hereby finds and declares that the
indiscriminate placement and use of recreational vehicles (RVs) on individual
lots within the City threatens the health and safety of citizens, and damages
property values. In order to protect property values, to preserve the intent of
the City's comprehensive plan, and to promote the general safety and welfare of
the citizens of the City, recreational vehicles shall be located only within
approved recreation vehicle parks, or as otherwise allowed in this ordinance
(see Section 4-512). (Ord. 210, 3-6-1995)
5-4-2: DEFINITIONS:
 
                      A wheeled vehicle less than ten (10) feet in width at its
RECREATIONAL VEHICLE: widest point, self-propelled or unpowered and/or
                      qualifying for a State of Idaho recreation vehicle
                      permit.
RV PARK:              A tract of land with one or more spaces rented for the
                      parking of recreational vehicles. (Ord. 210, 3-6-1995)
 
5-4-3: APPLICATION AND PERMITS:
   A.   A permit is required to operate or maintain any recreational vehicle
park. Applications for such permits shall be made to the Planning and Zoning
Commission through the City Clerk. The Commission shall then enact upon the
application after such notice and hearing as required by law, and make its
recommendations to the City Council, who shall then either grant or deny said
application.
   B.   No recreational vehicle park permit shall be transferrable. Every
person holding such a permit shall give notice in writing to the City within
five (5) days after having sold, transferred or otherwise disposed of any
interest in, or control of an RV facility, unless a new permit has been granted
to subsequent owners or if any application for a new permit is pending.
   Applications for permits by prospective new owners may be made in advance of
any sale or transfer, and shall be approved if the terms of the applicable
ordinances are met.
   C.   A recreational vehicle park permit holder shall maintain a current plot
plan of each recreational vehicle park and ensure that such current plot plan
is in file with the City Clerk.
   D.   The City Council is hereby authorized to revoke or suspend any
recreational vehicle park permit issued hereunder if, after due investigation,
it determines that the holder thereof has violated any of the provisions of
this chapter or that any recreational vehicle park is being maintained or
operated in an unsanitary or unsafe manner, or, because of the manner of
operation constitutes a public nuisance. (Ord. 210, 3-6-1995)
5-4-4: REQUIREMENT FOR RECREATIONAL VEHICLE PARKS:
   A.   Alteration or enlargement. Recreational vehicle parks in use as of the
effective date of this ordinance shall be permitted to continue as an
established land use, but shall not be altered, in either construction or
operation, so as to cause any deviation from the minimum standards of this
Chapter, insofar as the pre-existing use complies with this chapter on the
effective date hereof. If a non-conforming recreational vehicle park is
enlarged in either area or in usage (e.g. number of spaces available for rental
or an increase in seasonal availability of rental spaces), the entire park
shall be subject to the provisions hereof, specifically including, but not
limited to, the standards herein and the requirements of a permit.
   B.   Records required. Every recreational vehicle park shall at all items
keep a register of all guests or tenants which shall be open to inspection by
State, Federal and City officials. Said register shall contain the following
information:
      1.   Names and addresses of each guest tenant.
      2.   Dates of entrance and departure.
      3.   Vehicle registration numbers and state of issue of each recreational
vehicle and tow vehicle.
   C.   Maintenance. Each recreational vehicle park shall be kept in a clean,
orderly and sanitary condition at all times.
   D.   Fire protection. Each recreational vehicle park shall be subject to
inspection by the City Fire Chief and shall and maintain fire protection
equipment such as fire extinguishers, fire hydrants and other equipment in such
quantities and locations as specified by said Fire Chief, and as may be
necessary to meet all applicable building and life safety codes. Open fires
shall not be allowed in a recreational vehicle park except in locations and in
facilities approved by the Fire Chief.
   E.   Interior park drives: All spaces within the recreational vehicle park
shall have direct access to an interior roadway not less than twenty-five feet
(25') in width which shall have unobstructed access to a public street or
highway. Dead-end roadways shall provide adequate vehicle turning space, or a
cul-de-sac with not less than a fifty-two foot (52') diameter exclusive of
parking.
   F.   Landscaping and screening. The recreational vehicle park boundaries
shall be reasonably screened from outside view, whether by barriers of
ornamental fences, walls, trees or shrubs to assure reasonable integration with
adjoining land usages and to assure the health, safety and quiet enjoyment of
the area.
   G.   Occupant improvement. Recreational vehicle parks space occupants shall
be not permitted to erect or install any structures.
   H.   Utilities. All recreational vehicle park spaces will be serviced by
water, sewer and electrical hookups. Generators on individual recreational
vehicles will not be allowed to operate between the hours of 7:00 p.m. and 9:00
a.m.
   I.   Storage of hazardous material. Storage of hazardous or potentially
hazardous materials shall not be allowed beneath recreational vehicles.
Hazardous or potentially hazardous materials include, but are not limited to,
flammable liquids, combustible liquids, compressed gas, combustible waste
matter, fireworks, firearms, or ammunition. (Ord. 210, 3-6-1995)
TITLE 6
PUBLIC UTILITIES
CHAPTER 1
UTILITY SERVICES
SECTION:
6-1-1: Definitions
6-1-2: Utility Service Billing
6-1-3: Payment Of Charges; Delinquencies; Water Shutoff
6-1-4: Conditions For Discontinuance Of Refuse Service
6-1-5: Penalty
6-1-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
UTILITY CHARGE: The fee, rental, rate, charge, service charge or assessment
provided for in this Code as reimbursement to the City for rendering to the
utility user of the services of that particular utility for which the charge is
made.
UTILITY SERVICE: The Municipal water service, and the Municipal refuse service,
and the Municipal sewer service are each defined as utility services of the
City of Winchester.
UTILITY SERVICE BILL: The statement containing the combined total amounts of
all utility charges due and payable to the City for utility services furnished
and delinquency charges assessed.
UTILITY USER: The owner of the property, or a renter, tenant or other nonowner
occupant of the property, to which one, or all the utility services of the
City, is supplied.
(1990 Code §8-201; amd. 2018 Code)
6-1-2: UTILITY SERVICE BILLING:
   A.   Billing To Property Owners: Unless otherwise provided herein, all
utility services of the City shall be billed to the owner of the property to
which the utility services of the City are supplied. (1990 Code §8-202)
   B.   Billing To Tenants:
      1.   If any utility user as defined in section 6-1-1 of this chapter
desires the utility services to be billed to a renter, tenant or other nonowner
occupant of the property, the property owner may enter into a contractual
guarantee agreement with the City, whereupon the City may bill directly to the
tenant until further notice so long as the payments are current. Any such
practice shall be as a convenience to the property owner only and shall not
relieve the owner of responsibility for payment heretofore imposed.
      2.   The authority to enter into such agreements on behalf of the City is
hereby delegated to the City Council, to be on a standard form of agreement
approved by the City Council and filed thereafter with the City Clerk-
Treasurer. (1990 Code §8-207)
   C.   Monthly Billing:
      1.   Utility service billings shall be made monthly on an itemized
statement which shall contain the following information: period covered by
billings; water meter reading date; present water meter reading at billing
date; water meter reading at last billing; and a statement as to the amount of
water used or the estimated amount of water used.
      2.   In addition, the utility statement shall contain information in a
monetary amount as to the water rental due, or estimated due; water rental past
due; refuse services due, refuse services past due; sewer rental due; sewer
rental past due; and delinquency or service charge, if any.
      3.   The utility service bill shall then contain a total of all utility
charges due and payable to the City. (1990 Code §8-202)
   D.   Charges Not Prorated: If any utility service is supplied to a premises
for any portion of a calendar month, such utility service shall be billed to
the utility user for the entire month. No utility charge shall be prorated for
a portion of any month. (1990 Code §8-205)
6-1-3: PAYMENT OF CHARGES; DELINQUENCIES; WATER SHUTOFF:
   A.   Delinquency; Additional Monthly Charge; Lien:
      1.   All utility service bills are due and payable monthly on the first
day of the month following the month in which such services are used and shall
be delinquent if unpaid at the next billing date. If not paid before
delinquent, a charge of five dollars ($5.00) per month shall be added to the
amount previously due.
      2.   All utility charges and utility service charges provided for in this
Code, and the delinquency charges thereon, shall be a lien upon the property to
which utility services are rendered, superior to all other liens and
encumbrances whatsoever except for general taxes and local special assessments.
The City Clerk-Treasurer is hereby authorized and directed, prior to the
expiration of six (6) months from the first day of the first month for which
such charges are unpaid, to certify to the Auditor of Lewis County, all such
utility charges as a lien upon such property.
   B.   Water Shutoff For Nonpayment; Return To Service Fee: As an additional
and concurrent method of enforcing the lien of the City for said utility
charges when the same shall become delinquent and remain so for a period of
thirty (30) days, the City Clerk is hereby authorized and directed to cut off
the Municipal water service from the premises to which utility services were
furnished, and said service shall remain cut off until all of the utility
service bill, utility service charges, delinquency charges and a return to
service fee of fifty dollars ($50.00) have been paid in full. (Ord. 444, 6-13-
2005)
   C.   Shutoff Notice: Municipal water service shall be turned off at any such
premises for the nonpayment of any or all of the utility service on such date
as indicated on the utility bill. (Ord. 444, 6-13-2005; amd. 2018 Code)
6-1-4: CONDITIONS FOR DISCONTINUANCE OF REFUSE SERVICE:
   A.   Procedure For Discontinuance:
      1.   Whenever any utility user desires to discontinue the Municipal
refuse service because the property to which such service is supplied has been
vacated or is uninhabited, or will be unused for a period of time, he shall
notify the City Clerk that he wishes such refuse service to be discontinued.
The utility user shall exhibit to the City Clerk his most recent utility
service bill showing that the utility services, as well as all service charges
have been paid to date. If all utility services and service charges have been
paid in full to date, the City Clerk shall notify all the appropriate City
departments that all the Municipal refuse service is to be discontinued, as
well as the date of its discontinuance.
      2.   Whenever a utility user desires to recommence the refuse service
discontinued as provided herein, the City Clerk shall notify all the
appropriate City departments that the Municipal refuse service is to be
reinstated to the utility user's premises and the date at which the refuse
service is to commence. (1990 Code §8-204; amd. 2018 Code)
      3.   No fee or service charge shall be assessed for any of the above
services. (1990 Code §8-204)
   B.   Billing Abated: All billings for refuse service upon the utility
service bill shall be abated and discontinued, and all refuse service shall be
discontinued until the utility user notifies the City Clerk that refuse service
should be reinstated. (1990 Code §8-204; amd. 2018 Code)
6-1-5: PENALTY:
Any person violating the provisions of this chapter shall, upon conviction
thereof, be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished pursuant to
section 1-4-1 of this Code. (1990 Code §8-206)
CHAPTER 2
WATER USE AND REGULATIONS
SECTION:
6-2-1: Definitions
6-2-2: Water Division Established; Supervision; Account Collection
6-2-3: Application For Water Connection; Fee
6-2-4: Water Meters
6-2-5: Service Connections And Service Pipes
6-2-6: Meters And Materials Property Of City
6-2-7: Water Service Rates And Charges
6-2-8: Turn Off Of Water; Turn On Charge
6-2-9: Newly Installed Services
6-2-10: Supplying Water To Others; Permit
6-2-11: Emergency Shutoff
6-2-12: Refusing Access To Premises
6-2-13: Irrigation Water Regulated
6-2-14: Water Use Restrictions
6-2-15: Penalty
6-2-1: DEFINITIONS:
Unless the context specifically indicates otherwise, the meanings of terms used
in this chapter shall be as follows:
DIRECTOR: The Public Works Director of the City of Winchester, his agent or
representative.
PERSON OR CONSUMER: Any individual, firm, company, association, society,
corporation or group.
PREMISES OR PROPERTY: The real property or buildings served or proposed to be
served by the City water system.
SHALL/MAY: "Shall" is mandatory; "may" is permissible.
WATER MAIN: A pipe or conduit for carrying domestic water.
WATER SYSTEM: All facilities for storing, pumping, treating and distributing of
water. (1990 Code §3-338)
6-2-2: WATER DIVISION ESTABLISHED; SUPERVISION; ACCOUNT COLLECTION:
   A.   Division Established: The Water Division of the Department of Public
Utilities of the City is hereby established. (1990 Code §3-301)
