   B.   Supervision: The Public Works Director shall have full supervision,
charge and control of the Water Division. He shall make and enforce such rules
as he may deem necessary for the efficient administration and regulation of the
division. (1990 Code §3-302; amd. 2018 Code)
6-2-3: APPLICATION FOR WATER CONNECTION; FEE:
   A.   Use Of Form: Any person, firm or corporation desiring to have property
connected with the water supply system of the City shall make an application
therefor to the Public Works Director on a printed form to be furnished to the
Water Division. (1990 Code §3-303; amd. 2018 Code)
   B.   Information; Agreement:
      1.   The application shall be made and signed by the owner or lessee of
the property, or the authorized agent of such owner or lessee, and shall fully
state:
         a.   All the purposes for which the water shall be used.
         b.   The number of service pipes desired.
         c.   Whether there shall be more than one building on more than one
separate property supplied by the one service connection with the City main.
         d.   The number, kind of buildings and properties so supplied.
         e.   Probable consumption.
         f.   The size of service pipe or connection believed to be necessary
therefor.
         g.   The name of the applicant, and whether the owner, authorized
agent or renter.
      2.   Such application shall contain an agreement that the applicant will
at all times conform to and be governed by the rules and regulations of the
Water Division and provisions of this chapter, and that he will pay for all
water used on the premises, at the rate supplied in said rules. (1990 Code §3-
304)
   C.   Minimum City Water Connection Fee: The minimum fee to be charged by the
City for the connection of City water to any privately owned property within
the corporate City limits shall be two thousand dollars ($2,000.00). (Ord., 10-
7-1996)
6-2-4: WATER METERS:
   A.   Installation In New Services: Whenever any new service shall be
installed connecting any property with the water supply system of the City, a
meter shall be installed with the service and water will be supplied to the
property through such meter only. (1990 Code §3-306)
   B.   Installation On Any Premises: Meters shall be installed on any premises
whatsoever, when, in the opinion of the Water Division, the installation of a
meter may for any just reason be deemed necessary. (1990 Code §3-307)
   C.   Meters Supplied By City: Meters shall be supplied by the City. (1990
Code §3-308)
   D.   Installation By Water Division: The actual installation of all meters
shall be done by the Water Division. (1990 Code §3-309)
   E.   Size And Design: All meters shall be of a standard size and design
approved by the Public Works Director and each meter shall, before it is
installed, be separately examined, tested and approved by him. (1990 Code §3-
310)
   F.   Testing Accuracy; Filing Of Request; Fee:
      1.   When the accuracy of the record of a water meter is questioned by
the consumer, the meter shall be removed at his request and shall be tested by
the Director in the presence of the consumer and a record kept thereof. Both
parties shall accept the findings so made. Before making such tests, the
consumer, at the time of filing his request, shall deposit with the Director
the sum of ten dollars ($10.00). If a test so made discloses an error against
the consumer of more than three percent (3%) in the meter register, the excess
of such reading as applied to the three (3) readings next preceding the test
shall be calculated and the amount of money due the consumer thereon credited
to his meter account. The Water Division shall bear the entire expense of the
test and the deposit of the consumer shall be returned to him. If no error in
excess of three percent (3%) against the consumer is found, the consumer shall
pay the cost of the test out of his deposit. No meter shall be removed or in
any way disturbed nor the seal broken except in the presence, and under the
supervision of the Director. (1990 Code §3-311)
      2.   In the event of a water meter getting out of order or failing to
register properly, the consumer shall be charged on an estimate made from the
most reliable date in the possession of the Water Division. (1990 Code §3-315)
   G.   Inspection Of Premises: The Water Division reserves the right to enter
at any reasonable time any premises where City water is used, for the purpose
of making an examination of the premises, or a test of the meter, and it also
reserves the right to remove the meter from the premises for examination and
test when necessary. (1990 Code §3-312)
   H.   Meters Property Of City; Location:
      1.   All meters shall be and remain the property of the City, and shall
not be removed from the service except for test or repair and replacement or on
abandonment or discontinuance of the service.
      2.   All meters shall be so located and maintained as to be readily
accessible at all reasonable hours for reading, inspection and repairs. (1990
Code §3-313)
   I.   Lost, Damaged Or Broken Meters; Cost Of Repair Or Replacement:
      1.   In cases where a meter has been lost, damaged or broken, by or
through the carelessness or negligence of the owner or the occupant of the
premises serviced, such meter shall be properly repaired and restored under the
direction of the Director and the cost thereof shall be charged against the
owner or occupant of the premises.
      2.   In cases of nonpayment of such charges, the water shall be turned
off and not again turned on until the cost of repairs and the penalty for
shutting off and turning on the water has been paid. (1990 Code §3-314)
6-2-5: SERVICE CONNECTIONS AND SERVICE PIPES:
   A.   Separate Connections Required: Every separate building supplied with
City water must have its own separate connection with the City mains, except
that two (2) or more buildings located on the same lot, or on contiguous lots
under a single ownership, may be, upon written permission granted by the
Director, supplied through the same connection with the City main in cases
where a water meter is installed in the service, as long as said single
ownership continues. Upon change from such single ownership, a new and separate
connection shall be immediately made for the building or premises theretofore
having the indirect connection. (1990 Code §3-316)
   B.   Location And Maintenance: All service pipes from the City mains or from
other City service pipes to the water meter and all water meters and
appurtenant structures shall be installed in accordance with the written
specifications to be established by the Public Works Director. These
specifications shall include material, depth, location, accessibility and
required and permitted fixtures. Such specifications shall be reduced to
writing and copies of the same shall be available for inspection or copying by
interested persons at the Office of the City Clerk-Treasurer. Such
specifications may be revised or amended from time to time by said Director as
changes of conditions or technology may warrant or as may be in the interests
of efficient operation of the water system. The owner of the property served
shall be responsible for the installation and maintenance of all service lines
and other plumbing downstream from the City meter, or if no meter, from the
property line. (Ord., 5-6-1991)
   C.   Unlawful Connections: It shall be unlawful for any person, except a
competent person authorized by the Director, to make any connection with a City
service pipe or with any part of the City water system. (1990 Code §3-318)
   D.   Unlawful Tampering With City Service Pipes: No person, other than the
Director or his authorized agent, shall use any street key or other device for
the purpose of shutting off water or turning on same outside of his property
line; nor shall any person uncover or attempt to uncover, or tamper with any
pipe, valve, meter, meter box, curb stop, or curb stop box of a City service
connection without the authority from the Director. (1990 Code §3-319)
   E.   Services Outside City Limits: No water mains shall be constructed or
laid by the City outside the City limits to any premises; provided, however,
mains may be laid to property belonging to the City. All proposed consumers who
have property outside the City limits and who desire to obtain City water shall
construct their own mains from the City limits to their own property at their
own expense. All City meters in such cases shall be placed as near as
practicable to the City limits. (1990 Code §3-337)
6-2-6: METERS AND MATERIALS PROPERTY OF CITY:
All meters furnished and all materials supplied by the Water Department in the
installation or repair of any meter or meters, and all materials supplied in
the installation of any service connection with the City mains, or in tapping
any City main, shall remain the property of the City and may be removed by the
Water Department at any time for nonpayment of any charges or installment due.
(1990 Code §3-332)
6-2-7: WATER SERVICE RATES AND CHARGES:
   A.   Monthly Service Charges: The rates and charges for water supplied by
the City water system shall be a monthly minimum charge of forty eight dollars
twenty six cents ($48.26) for the first three thousand (3,000) gallons or less.
(1990 Code §3-333; amd. 2018 Code)
   B.   Credit Allowed Fire Department Premises: All active members in good
standing of the Winchester Volunteer Fire Department shall be allowed a maximum
credit of forty eight dollars twenty six cents ($48.26) per month against their
water accounts. This credit shall not be accumulative, but shall be used in
full each month, nor shall this credit be in any way applied against the sewer
accounts. This sum is granted to them as partial consideration for their
services. The Fire Chief shall quarterly submit to the Director or the City
Clerk-Treasurer a list of all active members of the Volunteer Fire Department.
(1990 Code §§3-335, 3-342; amd. 2018 Code)
   C.   Nonresidents:
      1.   Surcharge On Nonresident Consumption: All water used by consumers on
premises located outside the City limits shall pay, in addition to the regular
rate charges set forth in subsection A of this section, a surcharge of twenty
five percent (25%) on all water furnished. This charge is made to partially
compensate the City for not obtaining tax money from the premises served, for
use on the water system. (1990 Code §3-334)
      2.   Contracts For Nonresident Consumption: All persons desiring water
service from the City to property located outside the corporate limits of the
City shall, as a condition of receiving such initial and/or continuing service,
enter into a contract with the City in a standard form to be approved by the
Mayor and Public Works Director to the effect that they shall be bound by all
City ordinances dealing with water service to the same extent as are residents
of the City, insofar as can be applied by law and where not inconsistent by the
terms of the individual ordinance. Provided, however, that neither this
subsection, nor subsection C1 of this section, shall constitute an enforceable
commitment by the City to furnish or an enforceable right on the part of
property owners to receive City water service outside the City, it being
understood that such service will only be provided and/or continued to the
extent that the system has water capacity available in excess of the needs of
the users inside the corporate limits, including fire protection, other public
uses and outside water contracts with priority. (Ord., 5-6-1991)
6-2-8: TURN OFF OF WATER; TURN ON CHARGE:
   A.   Unlawful Turning On Of Water: When water has been shut off from any
premises, either upon the application of the owner or occupant thereof, or for
nonpayment of water charges, or for any other cause, it shall be a misdemeanor
for any person to again connect such premises with the City water supply system
except when specifically authorized so to do by the Director; and the Director
may cause the water to be shut off at the main, or may remove a portion of the
service connection in the street. In addition to the penalty in this chapter
provided for violation of its provisions, the Water Department may also charge
to and collect from the owner or occupant of the premises so illegally
connected, the whole cost of the disconnection and reconnection, and the
penalty of fifty dollars ($50.00) for shutting off the water and for turning on
the water, the whole of such penalties and charges to be paid before the water
is again turned on. (1990 Code §3-320; amd. 2018 Code)
   B.   Service Charge For Turning On: Whenever water is turned off, except
upon the request of the owner or occupant of the premises, it shall not be
turned on until after the payment of a charge of fifty dollars ($50.00) for
said service, as provided in subsection A of this section. (1990 Code §3-321;
amd. 2018 Code)
6-2-9: NEWLY INSTALLED SERVICES:
In all cases where a water service has been newly installed connecting any
premises or building with the City mains, and in all cases of reconstruction,
alteration or repair of any building where new or additional water services or
fixtures have been installed, City water shall not be turned on to such service
until all charges for water used on the premises for any purpose shall have
been paid. (1990 Code §3-322)
6-2-10: SUPPLYING WATER TO OTHERS; PERMIT:
   A.   Permit Requirements:
      1.   No owner or lessee of property supplied with water from the City
mains shall furnish water to any other person or property without first
obtaining a written permit to do so from the Public Works Director. No permit
will be issued until the person desiring to use the water has obtained and
filed with the Director a written consent of the owner or lessee of the
property from which the water is to be taken, stating the location of such
property by street and number, and the location by street and number of the
property to be supplied with water, and stating the purpose for which the water
is to be used.
      2.   Upon receipt of a proper permit as herein provided, from the owner
or lessee of the property from which the water is to be taken, and, where water
is taken from premises paying a flat rate, upon payment in advance for the
water for the whole term for which the permit is issued, the Director may issue
a temporary permit allowing water to be supplied to other persons or property
for domestic and other purposes, but no permit shall be issued for a longer
time than three (3) months.
   B.   Violation: Any person allowing water to be taken from the premises
owned or occupied by him by any person without such person having a permit from
the Director shall be in violation of this chapter. (1990 Code §3-323)
6-2-11: EMERGENCY SHUTOFF:
The Public Works Director may, in an emergency, order the water cut off from
any premises connected with the City mains, without notice, for repairs or
other necessary purposes. The City will not be liable for any damage that may
occur on account of the water being cut off for any of the above purposes, or
on account of the breaking of any pipe or fixture by pressure of the water from
the City mains. (1990 Code §3-324)
6-2-12: REFUSING ACCESS TO PREMISES:
   A.   Prohibition: It shall be unlawful for any person to refuse, neglect or
fail to afford any duly authorized representative of the Water Department free
access at all reasonable hours to any and all parts of buildings or premises
supplied with water from the City water supply system, for the purpose of
making records, readings and inspections of the location, condition and
sufficiently of pipes, fittings, valves, cocks, fixtures and appliances, and
noting the amount of water used and the manner in which it is used.
   B.   Violation: Violation of this provision, or the abuse, threatening or
attempted intimidation of any officer of the Water Department, may result in
the shutting off of the water and the imposition of the usual penalties in
addition to punishment for violation of this chapter as elsewhere herein
provided. (1990 Code §3-325)
6-2-13: IRRIGATION WATER REGULATED:
   A.   City Authority:
      1.   To assure adequate supplies of water for purposes of domestic use
and firefighting, the City Council shall have the authority to promulgate and
declare reasonable restrictions upon the use of City water for the purposes of
irrigation of crops, lawns and all other outdoor horticultural uses. These
restrictions may include, but are not limited to, the prohibition of any
irrigation in the City for the time periods stated in the order, allowing
irrigation only during certain specified hours, allowing irrigation only on
specified days, allowing irrigation only for specified purposes of allowing
only the use of a specified maximum quantity of water for irrigation.
      2.   Any such restrictive orders issued by said City Council shall be
promulgated after a reasonable investigation and forecast of the quantity of
water available, the minimum needs and reserve required of water available, the
minimum needs and reserve required for other water usage, and the estimated
water usage to be avoided by the proposed order.
      3.   All such orders curtailing the unlimited use of water for irrigation
shall be limited in time, and shall not, unless expiring sooner by its own
terms, be effective for more than thirty (30) days after its issuance, unless
extended by City Council for good cause. (1990 Code §3-302A; amd. 2018 Code)
      4.   All such orders shall be posted at the City Hall and such other
places as are reasonably calculated to give notice to the public.
      5.   Any person knowingly violating the terms of an order promulgated
under this subsection shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished
accordingly. In addition to or in lieu of criminal prosecution, any person
knowingly violating such an order shall be liable for a civil penalty not
exceeding the sum of three hundred dollars ($300.00), which penalty shall be
assessed in the first instance by the City Council, and may be enforced in any
court of competent jurisdiction. Provided, however, that no person shall be
punished, criminally or civilly, unless it be demonstrated that such person
first had actual knowledge of the existence of the order and refused or
neglected to obey the same after a reasonable opportunity to comply. (1990 Code
§3-302A)
   B.   Irrigation Regulations:
      1.   Irrigation With Unmetered Services: On unmetered service, a moderate
amount of water for irrigation may be used, which privilege may be canceled by
the Director if water is used beyond a reasonable amount. (1990 Code §3-326)
      2.   Sprinkling Devices And Hoses: No water shall be used for irrigation
except through a nozzle, spray nozzle or other sprinkling device; and no hose
or sprinkling device shall be left running unattended. (1990 Code §3-327)
      3.   Prohibiting Irrigation: In case of shortage of water, the use of
water for irrigation may be prohibited by the Director. (1990 Code §3-328)
6-2-14: WATER USE RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Shortages And Emergencies: If any person refuses to comply with the
request of any employee of the Water Department to conserve water during a
shortage or emergency, water services may be discontinued. (1990 Code §3-330)
   B.   Use During Fires: It shall be unlawful for any person to use water for
irrigation or sprinkling during the progress of any fire in the City, except
for protection from fire, and all such irrigation and sprinkling shall be
immediately stopped when the fire alarm is sounded and not resumed until the
fire is out. (1990 Code §3-331)
6-2-15: PENALTY:
Any person found to be violating any provision of this chapter shall be served
by the City with written notice stating the nature of the violation and
providing a reasonable time limit for the satisfactory correction thereof. Any
offender who shall, within the period of time stated in such notice, not
permanently cease such violation shall, upon conviction thereof, be deemed
guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished pursuant to section
1-4-1 of this Code. (1990 Code §3-339)
CHAPTER 3
SEWER USE AND REGULATIONS
SECTION:
6-3-1: Definitions
6-3-2: Sewer Connection Fee And Service Charges
6-3-3: Use Of Public Sewers Required; Restrictions
6-3-4: Building Sewers And Connections
6-3-5: Prohibited Discharges
6-3-6: Protection From Damage
6-3-7: Right Of Entry For Inspection
6-3-8: Penalty
6-3-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
BUILDING DRAIN: That part of the lowest horizontal piping of a drainage system
which receives the discharge from soil, waste, and other drainage pipes inside
the walls of the building and conveys it to the building sewer, beginning six
feet (6') outside the inner face of the building wall.
COMBINED SEWER: A sewer receiving both surface runoff and sewage.
DIRECTOR: The Public Works Director of the City of Winchester, or his
authorized deputy, agent or representative.
GARBAGE: Solid wastes from the preparation, cooking, and dispensing of food,
and from the handling, storage, and sale of produce.
INDUSTRIAL WASTES: The liquid wastes from industrial processes as distinct from
sanitary sewage.
NATURAL OUTLET: Any outlet into a watercourse, pond, ditch, lake or other body
of surface water or groundwater.
PERSON: Any individual, firm, company, association, society, corporation or
group.
PROPERLY SHREDDED GARBAGE: The wastes from the preparation, cooking, and
dispensing of food that have been shredded to such degree that all particles
will be carried freely under the flow conditions normally prevailing in public
sewers, with no particle greater than one-fourth inch (1/4") in any dimension.
PUBLIC SEWER: A sewer in which all owners of abutting properties have equal
rights, and is controlled by public authority.
SANITARY SEWER: A sewer which carries sewage and to which stormwater, surface
water, and groundwater are not intentionally admitted.
SEWAGE: A combination of the water carried wastes from residences, business
buildings, institutions, and industrial establishments, together with such
groundwater, surface water and stormwater as may be present.
SEWAGE TREATMENT PLANT: Any arrangement of devices and structures used for
treating sewage.
SEWAGE WORKS: All facilities for collecting, pumping, treating, and disposing
of sewage.
SEWER: A pipe or conduit for carrying sewage.
SHALL/MAY: "Shall" is mandatory; "may" is permissive.
STORM SEWER OR STORM DRAIN: A sewer which carries stormwater and surface water
and drainage, but excludes sewage and polluted industrial wastes.
SUSPENDED SOLIDS: Solids that either float on the surface of, or are in
suspension in, water, sewage, or other liquids, and which are removable by
laboratory filtering.
WATERCOURSE: A channel in which a flow of water occurs, either continuously or
intermittently. (1990 Code §3-401)
6-3-2: SEWER CONNECTION FEE AND SERVICE CHARGES:
   A.   Connection Fee: A connection charge of one thousand dollars ($1,000.00)
is hereby established and assessed against each premises connecting onto the
City sewer system. (Ord., 10-7-1996)
   B.   Rates For Sewer Service: The following minimum rates and charges are
hereby fixed for sewage service furnished by the City, and shall be paid
therefor as follows:
 
Residential      $44.05 per EDU
Commercial       44.05 per EDU
Multi-commercial 44.05 per EDU
RV dump station  44.05 per EDU
 
(1990 Code §3-410; amd. 2018 Code)
6-3-3: USE OF PUBLIC SEWERS REQUIRED; RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Connection Required: The owners of all houses, buildings or properties
used for human occupancy, employment, recreation, or other purpose, situated
within the City and abutting on any street, alley or right-of-way in which
there is now located or may in the future be located a public sanitary or
combined sewer of the City, is hereby required at his expense to install
suitable toilet facilities therein, and to connect all building drains directly
with the proper public sewer in accordance with the provisions of this chapter,
within thirty (30) days after date of official notice to do so; provided, that
said public sewer is within two hundred feet (200') of the property line.
   B.   Prohibited Acts:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person to place, deposit, or permit to
be deposited in an insanitary manner upon public or private property within the
City, or in any area under the jurisdiction of the City, any human or animal
excrement, garbage or other objectionable waste.
      2.   It shall be unlawful to discharge to any natural outlet within the
City, or in any area under the jurisdiction of the City, sanitary sewage,
industrial wastes, or other polluted waters, except where suitable treatment
has been provided in accordance with subsequent provision of this chapter.
      3.   Except as hereinafter provided, it shall be unlawful to construct or
maintain any privy, privy vault, septic tank, cesspool or other facility
intended or used for the disposal of sewage. (1990 Code §3-402)
6-3-4: BUILDING SEWERS AND CONNECTIONS:
   A.   Permit Required; Classifications:
      1.   No authorized person shall uncover, make any connections with or
opening into, use, alter, or disturb and public sewer or appurtenance thereof
without first obtaining a written permit from the Director.
      2.   There shall be the following classes of building sewer permits: a)
for residential and commercial service; and b) for service to establishments
producing industrial wastes. In either case, the owner or his agent shall make
application on a special form furnished by the City. The permit application
shall be supplemented by any plans, specifications, or other information
considered pertinent in the judgment of the Director.
   B.   Costs Borne By Owner: All costs and expense incident to the
installation and connection of the building sewer shall be borne by the owner.
The owner shall indemnify the City from any loss or damage that may directly or
indirectly be occasioned by the installation of the building sewer.
   C.   Separate Sewer For Each Building; Exception: A separate and independent
building sewer shall be provided for every building; except where one building
stands at the rear of another on an interior lot and no private sewer is
available or can be constructed to the rear building through an adjoining
alley, court, yard, or driveway, the building sewer from the front building may
be extended to the rear building and the whole considered as one building
sewer.
   D.   Old Building Sewers Used With New Buildings: Old building sewers may be
used in connection with new buildings only when they are found, on examination
and tested by the Director, to meet all requirements of this chapter. (1990
Code §3-404)
   E.   Construction And Excavation Requirements:
      1.   The building sewer shall be a four inch (4") ABS (plastic) pipe
schedule 40, no smaller, or other suitable material approved by the Director.
Joints shall be tight and waterproof. Any part of the building sewer that is
located within ten feet (10') of a water service pipe shall be constructed of
nonmetallic material if laid on a suitable bed or cradle as approved by the
Director.
      2.   The building drain shall extend six feet (6') outside the inner face
of the building wall at which point it shall connect the building sewer. The
minimum size of any building drain shall be determined on the basis of the
total number of fixture units drained, but in no case shall the building sewer
be less than four inches (4"). The slope of such four inch (4") pipe shall be
not less than one-fourth inch (1/4") per foot. (1990 Code §3-404; amd. 2018
Code)
      3.   Whenever possible, the building sewer shall be brought to the
building at an elevation below the basement floor. No building sewer shall be
laid parallel to or within three feet (3') of any bearing wall, which might
thereby be weakened. The depth shall be sufficient to afford protection from
frost. The building sewer shall be laid at uniform grade and in straight
alignment insofar as possible. Changes in direction shall be made only with
properly curved pipe and fittings.
      4.   In all buildings in which any building drain is too low to permit
gravity flow to the public sewer, sanitary sewage carried by such drain shall
be lifted by approved artificial means and discharged to the building sewer.
Drainage piping serving fixtures within a building location below the crown
level of the main sewer shall discharge into an approved watertight sump or
receiving tank, so located as to receive the sewage or wastes by gravity. From
such sump or receiving tank the sewage or other liquid wastes shall be lifted
and discharged into the house drain or house sewer or ejectors, pumps or other
equally efficient approved mechanical device.
      5.   The discharge line from such ejector, pump, or other mechanical
device shall be provided with an accessible backwater valve and gate valve, and
if the gravity drainage line to which such discharge line connects is
horizontal, the method of connection shall be from the top through a "Y" branch
fitting.
      6.   All backwater valves, gate valves, motors, compressors, air tanks,
or other mechanical devices shall be located where they will be accessible for
inspection and repair at all times, and unless continuously exposed, shall be
enclosed in a watertight masonry pit, fitted with a removable cover. The pipe
leading to an ejector or other appliance for raising sewage or other waste
matter to the street sewer shall, where a water closet or closets are
installed, be provided with a vent pipe not less than three inches (3") in
diameter, and where fixtures other than water closets are installed, the waste
vent pipe shall be the same diameter as the waste pipe. (1990 Code §3-404)
      7.   All sumps and receiving tanks shall be constructed of concrete or
Fiberglas pipe. If constructed of concrete, the walls and bottom shall be not
less than six inches (6") thick. Metal sumps and receiving tanks shall be of
such thickness as to serve the purpose for which they are intended, and shall
be painted inside and outside with corrosion resisting paint. All such sumps
and receiving tanks shall be automatically discharged. All sumps and receiving
tanks shall be provided with substantial and tight covers having a manhole that
will permit access to the tank for repairs and cleaning. Air tanks shall be so
proportioned as to be of equal cubical capacity to the ejectors connected
therewith in which there shall be maintained an air pressure of not less than
two (2) pounds for each foot of height the sewage is to be raised. No water-
operated ejectors shall be permitted. (1990 Code §3-404; amd. 2018 Code)
      8.   When subsoil drainage systems are installed, they shall discharge
into an approved sump or receiving tank entirely separate and independent of
any other drainage piping. Automatic mechanical ejectors or pumps shall be used
to lift the drainage from such sump or receiving tank, and the discharge
therefrom shall terminate over a properly trapped and vented fixture of such
capacity as to prevent flooding. No water-operated ejectors shall be permitted.
      9.   All excavations required for the installation of a building sewer
shall be open trench work unless otherwise approved by the Director. Pipe
laying and backfill shall be performed in accordance with ASTM specification
(C12-19) except that no backfill shall be placed until the work has been
inspected and approved. All backfills across streets or alleys must be properly
tamped. (1990 Code §3-404)
      10.   All joints and connections shall be made gastight and watertight
and shall be not less than one inch (1") deep.
      11.   The connection of the building sewer into the public sewer shall be
made at the "Y" branch, if such branch is available at a suitable location.
When a "Y" branch is not properly located or available, a neat hole may be cut
into the public sewer to receive the building sewer, with entry in the
downstream direction at an angle of about forty five degrees (45°). The
building sewer shall enter or be connected to the public sewer in the top one-
half (1/2) of the public sewer. The connection to be made through a special
fitting which shall be the hub end of an action of the house sewer pipe cut off
or a V saddle type of connection, inserted into the tap opening of the main,
either type thoroughly caulked and cemented so as to make a tight and secure
joint.
      12.   In attaching this hub fitting to the main, the hub end of the pipe
shall be cut short enough so that the shoulder of the hub shall rest flush on
the main with the end of the pipe to extend into the immediate wall of the main
so that the end thereof shall be flush with the inner face of the said wall.
The end of said pipe shall be cut to conform to the arc of said inner wall.
Each system of piping shall be laid in a separate trench when practicable. If
water piping is laid in the same trench as the sewer, it shall be at least one
foot (1') above the top edge of the sewer and offset at least eighteen inches
(18") from the central line of the sewer.
      13.   Cleanouts shall be placed at the junction of the building drain and
the building sewer and at intervals in the building sewer not to exceed one
hundred feet (100') and at changes in direction of the building sewer of ninety
degrees (90°) or more. Where the depth of the building sewer is four feet (4')
or more, the cleanout shall consist of a "Y" branch and one- eighth (1/8) bend
or a vertical riser extending the cleanout to the surface of the ground. All
cleanouts shall be plugged with air and watertight cleanout fittings. Cleanout
fittings shall be of the same nominal size as the pipes they serve, up to and
including four inch (4") pipe, and not less than four inches (4") for larger
pipes. (1990 Code §3-404; amd. 2018 Code)
   F.   Inspection: The applicant for the building sewer permit shall notify
the Director when the building sewer is ready for inspection and connection to
the public sewer. The connection shall be made under the supervision of the
Director or his representative.
   G.   Guarding Excavations; Restoration Of Public Ways: All excavations for
building sewer installation shall be adequately guarded with barricades and
lights so as to protect the public from hazard. Streets, sidewalks, parkways
and other public property disturbed in the course of the work shall be restored
in a manner satisfactory to the City. (1990 Code §3-404)
6-3-5: PROHIBITED DISCHARGES:
   A.   Stormwater; Other Drainage: No person shall discharge or cause to be
discharged any stormwater, surface water, groundwater, roof runoff, subsurface
drainage, cooling water or unpolluted industrial process waters to any sanitary
sewer.
   B.   Hazardous Or Toxic Waters And Wastes: Except as hereinafter provided,
no person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any of the following
described waters or wastes to any public sewer:
      1.   Any liquid or vapor having a temperature higher than one hundred
fifty degrees Fahrenheit (150°F). (1990 Code §3-405)
      2.   Any water or waste which may contain fat, oil, or grease. (1990 Code
§3-405; amd. 2018 Code)
      3.   Any gasoline, benzene, naphtha, fuel oil, or other flammable or
explosive liquid, solid or gas.
      4.   Any garbage that has not been properly shredded.
      5.   Any ashes, cinders, sand, mud, straw, shavings, metal, glass, rags,
feathers, tar, plastics, wood, paunch manure, or any other solid or viscous
substance capable of causing obstruction to the flow in sewers or other
interference with the proper operation of the sewage works.
      6.   Any waters or wastes containing a toxic or poisonous substance in
sufficient quantity to injure or interfere with any sewage treatment process,
constitute a hazard to humans or animals, or create any hazard in the receiving
waters of the sewage treatment plant.
      7.   Any waters or wastes containing suspended solids of such character
and quantity that unusual attention or expense is required to handle such
materials at the sewage treatment plant.
      8.   Any noxious or malodorous gas or substance capable of creating a
public nuisance.
   C.   Grease, Oil And Sand Interceptors Required:
      1.   Grease, oil, and sand interceptors shall be provided when, in the
opinion of the Director they are necessary for the proper handling of liquid
wastes containing grease in excessive amounts, or any flammable wastes, sand,
and other harmful ingredients; except that such interceptors shall not be
required for private living quarters or dwelling units. All interceptors shall
be of a type and capacity and accessible for cleaning and inspection.
      2.   Grease and oil interceptors shall be constructed of impervious
materials capable of withstanding abrupt and extreme changes in temperature.
They shall be of substantial construction, watertight, and equipped with easily
removable covers which when bolted in place shall be gastight and watertight.
      3.   Where installed, all grease, oil and sand interceptors shall be
maintained by the owner, at his expense, in continuously efficient operation at
all times.
   D.   Maintaining Preliminary Treatment Facilities: Where preliminary
treatment facilities are provided for any waters or wastes, they shall be
maintained continuously in satisfactory and effective operation by the owner at
his expense.
   E.   Special Agreements: No statement contained in this section shall be
construed as preventing any special agreement or arrangement between the City
and any industrial concern whereby an industrial waste of unusual strength or
character may be accepted by the City for treatment, subject to payment
therefor by the industrial concern. (1990 Code §3-405)
6-3-6: PROTECTION FROM DAMAGE:
No person shall maliciously, wilfully, or negligently break, damage, destroy,
uncover, deface or tamper with any structure, appurtenance, or equipment which
is a part of the Municipal sewage works. Any person violating this provision
shall be subject to immediate arrest under charge of disorderly conduct. (1990
Code §3-406; amd. 2018 Code)
6-3-7: RIGHT OF ENTRY FOR INSPECTION:
The Director and other duly authorized employees of the City bearing proper
credentials and identification shall be permitted to enter upon all properties
for the purpose of inspection, observation, measurement, sampling, and testing,
in accordance with the provisions of this chapter. (1990 Code §3-407)
6-3-8: PENALTY:
Any person found to be violating any provision of this chapter shall be served
by the City with written notice stating the nature of the violation and
providing a reasonable time limit for the satisfactory correction thereof. Any
offender who shall, within the period of time stated in such notice, not
permanently cease such violation shall, upon conviction thereof, be deemed
guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished pursuant to section
1-4-1 of this Code. (1990 Code §3-408)
CHAPTER 4
SOLID WASTE COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL
SECTION:
6-4-1: Purpose
6-4-2: Definitions
6-4-3: System Established
6-4-4: Compulsory Use
6-4-5: Collection Fees
6-4-6: Refuse Fund
6-4-7: Burning And Dumping
6-4-8: Refuse Containers
6-4-9: Rubbish, Special Handling
6-4-10: Vacated Premises
6-4-11: Collection Period
6-4-12: Inspection
6-4-13: Means Of Collection
6-4-14: Materials Not Acceptable For Collection
6-4-15: Vehicles Used For Collection
6-4-16: Penalty
6-4-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to eliminate unhealthy, unsanitary and unsightly
conditions in the City caused by the deposit and accumulation of refuse. (1990
Code §8-101)
6-4-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section. Certain words not defined herein shall be
defined as provided in section
1-3-2 of this Code; all other words shall be given the meanings ordinarily
applied to such words.
COLLECTOR: The person holding a contract with the City of Winchester for the
collection of garbage and refuse, or the person employed by the City of
Winchester and thereby authorized and designated by the City to collect,
handle, transport and dispose of refuse and waste.
GARBAGE:
   A.   "Garbage" shall include all putrescible waste, including waste
accumulated of animal, food, or vegetable matter, and including waste that
attends the preparation, use, cooking, dealing in or storing of meat, fish,
fowl, fruit and vegetables, and shall include all of such wastes or
accumulations of vegetable matter of residences, restaurants, hotels and places
where food is prepared for human consumption.
   B.   "Garbage" shall not include sewage and human waste or recognized
industrial byproducts.
INSPECTOR: The authorized employee or employees of the City of Winchester, or
some individual designated by the City Council as having the duty of the
enforcement of this chapter.
OWNER AND OCCUPANT: The terms "owner" and "occupant" may be used
interchangeably, and shall mean every person in possession, charge or in
control of any dwelling, flat, rooming house, or any eating place, shop, place
of business, manufacturing or business establishment where garbage or other
refuse is created or accumulated.
REFUSE: Solid wastes, including garbage and rubbish.
RUBBISH: Refuse other than garbage (such as: tin cans, bottles, ashes, paper,
pasteboard, cardboard or wooden boxes, brush, leaves, weeds, and cuttings from
trees, lawns, gardens and shrubs) produced in the normal course of doing
business or everyday living.
WASTE: Unwanted solid, liquid, or gaseous materials. (1990 Code §8-102)
6-4-3: SYSTEM ESTABLISHED:
   A.   There is hereby established a system of refuse collection,
transportation and disposal. It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in
the business of collection, transporting, hauling or conveying any refuse over
the streets or alleys, or to dump or dispose of the same unless and until such
person has a contract therefor as an authorized representative of the City.
   B.   This regulation does not prohibit a person from hauling or transporting
extra loads or accumulations of rubbish from the premises owned or occupied by
said person to one of the official disposal sites of the City that may be
hereafter established. (1990 Code §8-103)
6-4-4: COMPULSORY USE:
   A.   Every owner or occupant of the premises within the prescribed limits of
the City must use the refuse collection and disposal system herein provided,
and shall deposit or cause to be deposited in accordance with this chapter, all
rubbish and garbage.
   B.   The failure of any person to use the collection and disposal system
herein provided shall not exempt such person from the payment of the charges as
set forth in the rules and regulations on refuse control, save and except for
the provisions as set forth in this chapter. (1990 Code §8-104)
6-4-5: COLLECTION FEES:
   A.   The fees, rates and charges for collection of garbage and refuse within
the City are hereby fixed and determined to be those charges set forth in that
certain contract between the City of Winchester and Walco, Inc., dated January
1, 1991, any amendments duly made hereafter to that contract, or any subsequent
contract for solid waste disposal that shall hereafter be made and shall
hereafter be in force.
   B.   Provided, however, that where the enforcement of the provisions of this
chapter will work a financial hardship, or where the garbage and refuse is of
such small amounts as to not warrant the collection of the full fees and
charges as provided by this chapter, the City Council may issue a special
permit altering the provisions or this chapter and the fees and rates herein
set forth. (1990 Code §8-110)
6-4-6: REFUSE FUND:
The proceeds from the collection of fees and charges herein provided shall be
placed in a special fund to be known as the Refuse Service Revenue Fund, and
all payments to the refuse contractor and direct expenses of the City in the
operation of the refuse collection and disposal system shall be paid out of
such fund, and any surpluses remaining therein may be transferred by the City
Clerk-Treasurer to the General Fund of the City. (1990 Code §8-111)
6-4-7: BURNING AND DUMPING:
No person shall burn, incinerate, bury, dump, collect, remove or in any other
manner dispose of rubbish or garbage except as hereinafter provided:
   A.   Interior Incinerator: Any person, firm or corporation may use an
incinerator in the interior of a building between the hours of seven o'clock
(7:00) A.M. and seven o'clock (7:00) P.M. for rubbish, provided such
incinerator meets the requirements of the Building Code.
   B.   Exterior Incinerator: Burning of rubbish will be allowed in exterior
incinerators between the hours of nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. and nine o'clock (9:
00) P.M. Such incinerators shall be built of noncombustible material of not
lighter than one- eighth inch (1/8") metal, block or brick, covered by one inch
(1") wire mesh screen. Nothing herein contained shall be construed to prohibit
the use of outdoor fireplaces, barbecue pits or grills, in preparing food or
for recreational purposes.
   C.   Open Burning; Permit: Burning of rubbish may be done in vacant lots by
the owner thereof upon obtaining a permit from the Fire Department for such
burning. (1990 Code §8-105)
6-4-8: REFUSE CONTAINERS:
   A.   It shall be the duty of every owner or occupant of any place where
garbage or rubbish is created or accumulated to at all times keep or cause to
be kept portable approved containers for the deposit therein of rubbish and
garbage; and, except as otherwise provided, to deposit or cause to be deposited
all rubbish and garbage therein. All garbage shall, before deposit in such can,
be wrapped in paper or other material so as to prevent the escape of liquids
therefrom.
   B.   All such containers shall be watertight and not easily corrodible,
rodentproof and flyproof, shall be equipped with handles and a close fitting
lid. Such containers shall be not less than ten (10) gallons' capacity, nor
more than thirty two (32) gallons' capacity. The combined weight of any refuse
container and its contents shall not exceed seventy five (75) pounds. All metal
containers shall be of not less than twenty eight (28) gauge metal or the
equivalent, and be hot dipped after fabrication to assure nonleaking cans. All
other containers must be guaranteed by the manufacturer and so labeled to be
leakproof regardless of manufacturing processes. Such lid shall not be removed
except when necessary to place garbage and rubbish in such container or to take
the same therefrom. Whenever garbage or rubbish is placed therein or taken
therefrom, such lid shall be replaced by the person placing therein or taking
therefrom such garbage or rubbish. Such containers shall be kept in sanitary
conditions, with the inside and outside thereof washed at such times as to keep
the same free and clean of all accumulating grease and decomposing material and
so that no odor nuisance shall exist.
   C.   All garbage or refuse cans shall be placed in a place accessible to the
collector; provided, that in the case of isolated dwellings or places of
business or where reasonable access cannot be had by a truck, the cans may be
kept in such places as may be agreed upon by the owner and collector, or at
such place as may be designated by the inspector. Where there is no alley
entrance, such cans shall be placed and adjacent to street curb on collection
days. (1990 Code §8-106)
6-4-9: RUBBISH, SPECIAL HANDLING:
Rubbish consisting only of cardboard or wooden boxes, brush, leaves, wood and
cuttings from trees, lawns, shrubs and gardens, may be kept separately without
depositing in such containers; provided, that bulk materials, such as leaves,
shall be in a can, box, sack or receptacle for ease of loading and that brush,
etc., shall be cut in lengths not more than four feet (4') long, and tied in
bundles. Compost piles may be maintained for fertilization purposes and matter
used for fertilization purposes only may be transported, kept, and used.
Nothing in this section shall be construed so as to permit the violation of any
ordinance or any rule or regulation of the Fire Department of the City. (1990
Code §8-107)
6-4-10: VACATED PREMISES:
It shall be unlawful for any person, upon vacating or removing from dwellings,
storerooms or any other building situated in the City, to fail to remove all
garbage and rubbish from such building and premises, and also the grounds
appurtenant thereto; or to fail to place the same in a thoroughly sanitary
condition within twenty four (24) hours after the said premises shall be
vacated. (1990 Code §8-108)
6-4-11: COLLECTION PERIOD:
Collectors shall collect rubbish and garbage from each customer at least once
each week, or as may otherwise be provided by the rules and regulations of the
City Council. (1990 Code §8-109)
6-4-12: INSPECTION:
The City personnel or such other person as may be designated as sanitary
inspector, or any other person concerned with the enforcement of laws, shall
have the right of ingress and egress to any premises for the purpose or
inspection of places and containers where rubbish or garbage is accumulated or
kept. (1990 Code §8-112)
6-4-13: MEANS OF COLLECTION:
   A.   It shall be optional whether the City collects garbage and rubbish with
its own equipment and employees, or makes a contract with a person to collect
garbage and rubbish. The City Council shall, by resolution, elect the method or
methods to be used in the collection of garbage and rubbish. The Mayor shall be
the sole authority to contract or perform all services pertaining to refuse
collection and disposal, and is hereby authorized to enter into contracts with
one or more contractors and establish reasonable rules and regulations
governing the conduct and operation of such contracts.
   B.   The City Council may require of any such contractor, a bond in a
reasonable amount, the condition of which shall be the satisfactory performance
of the contract. (1990 Code §8-113)
6-4-14: MATERIALS NOT ACCEPTABLE FOR COLLECTION:
Dirt or earth debris from construction or lawn renovation, rocks, stones,
automobile bodies and parts, dead animals, building materials such as masonry,
plaster, scrap lumber and wood shavings, are not acceptable for collection, and
such items shall be collected and disposed of by the building contractor, owner
or occupants of the premises. (1990 Code §8-114)
6-4-15: VEHICLES USED FOR COLLECTION:
All collectors shall furnish vehicles designed for the collection and hauling
of garbage and rubbish. The collector shall keep such vehicles clean, sanitary,
neatly painted and in good running order, and shall wash, clean and disinfect
all such vehicles at least once a week. Each vehicle shall be equipped with a
tight metal body, or if a wooden body, shall be metal lined so as to be
watertight, and each vehicle shall at all times be provided with a suitable
cover securely fastened in such a manner as to retain dust and prevent the
scattering or dropping of rubbish or garbage upon public or private property.
(1990 Code §8-115)
6-4-16: PENALTY:
Any person violating the provisions of this chapter shall, upon conviction
thereof, be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished pursuant to
section
1-4-1 of this Code. (1990 Code §8-116)
TITLE 7
BUILDING AND DEVELOPMENT
CHAPTER 1
COMPREHENSIVE PLAN
SECTION:
7-1-1: Purpose
7-1-2: Identification Of Applicable Comprehensive Plan
7-1-3: Public Availability Of Plan
7-1-4: Amendment Of Comprehensive Plan
7-1-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of adopting a comprehensive plan is to provide for public officials
and private citizens a guide for making decisions that affect the future of the
City of Winchester. In order to avoid adverse effects of unplanned growth, the
comprehensive plan provides guidelines, policies and goals for logical growth.
The comprehensive plan provides the basis on which future zoning ordinances and
amendments can be based. (1990 Code §4-601)
7-1-2: IDENTIFICATION OF APPLICABLE COMPREHENSIVE PLAN:
The comprehensive plan that is officially adopted by the City by this reference
is the plan dated January 1980, certified copies of which are filed at the
Office of the City Clerk- Treasurer. (1990 Code §4-602; amd. 2018 Code)
7-1-3: PUBLIC AVAILABILITY OF PLAN:
Not less than three (3) copies of such comprehensive plan duly certified by the
City Clerk-Treasurer, have been filed for use and examination by the public in
the Office of the City Clerk- Treasurer. (1990 Code §4-603)
7-1-4: AMENDMENT OF COMPREHENSIVE PLAN:
Pursuant to Idaho Code section 67-6509(d), any person may petition and
recommend amendments to the comprehensive plan at any time. The Council will
review the request and follow proper amendment procedures if they feel it is in
the best interest of the City.
(1990 Code §4-604; amd. 2018 Code)
CHAPTER 2
AREA OF CITY IMPACT
SECTION:
7-2-1: Purpose
7-2-2: Geographic Area Of City Impact
7-2-3: Designation Of Permitted Use
7-2-4: Comprehensive Plan And Zoning Ordinance
7-2-5: Subdivision Ordinance
7-2-6: Review And Comment; Approval
7-2-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of establishing an Area of City Impact is to identify a logical
fringe area adjoining the City of Winchester and place it under appropriate
land development regulation. The fringe area includes the incorporated area
surrounding Winchester that has a potential for development and that could
affect the provision of public services or the quality of life in the City.
(1990 Code §4-701)
7-2-2: GEOGRAPHIC AREA OF CITY IMPACT:
The officially adopted geographic Area of City Impact includes all
unincorporated land within Section 31 and 32, T. 34N. R. 2W; and Section 5 and
6, T. 33N, R. 2W. All parcels of land, or portions thereof, lying within the
Area of City Impact shall be subject to provisions of this chapter. (1990 Code
§4-702)
7-2-3: DESIGNATION OF PERMITTED USE:
The geographical Area of City Impact as defined by the ordinances of the City
shall be designated and zoned as agricultural. Likewise, the comprehensive plan
and zoning ordinances of the City are amended to provide for such use. (1990
Code §4-703)
7-2-4: COMPREHENSIVE PLAN AND ZONING ORDINANCE:
The comprehensive plan and the zoning ordinance, and subsequent amendments
thereto, as officially adopted by the City Council shall apply to the Area of
City Impact. (1990 Code §4-704)
7-2-5: SUBDIVISION ORDINANCE:
Pursuant to Idaho Code section 50-1308, the subdivision ordinance and
subsequent amendments thereto as officially adopted by the City Council shall
apply to all plats situated within one mile outside of the City limits. The
subdivision ordinance and subsequent amendments thereto as officially adopted
by the Board of County Commissioners shall also apply to all other plats
situated within the Area of City Impact. (1990 Code §4-705)
7-2-6: REVIEW AND COMMENT; APPROVAL:
Any request for development, zone change, conditional use permit, or variance
within the Area of City Impact shall initially be referred to the Board of
County Commissioners, Lewis County, Idaho, for review and comment. The County
Commissioners shall have forty (40) days to consider the request, and submit a
reply to the City Council. If no reply is received by the Council within the
forty (40) day period, the Board forfeits its right to comment on the request,
and processing shall continue under the City's administration. Both the City
Council and Board shall approve all subdivision plats within the Area of City
Impact, pursuant to Idaho Code sections 50-1306 and 50-1308. (1990 Code §4-706)
CHAPTER 3
BUILDING CODES AND REGULATIONS
SECTION:
7-3-1: Adoption Of Building Codes
7-3-2: Definitions
7-3-3: Right Of Entry
7-3-4: Building Permit Fees
7-3-5: Penalty
7-3-1: ADOPTION OF BUILDING CODES:
   A.   Codes Adopted: There is hereby adopted by the City, for the purpose of
establishing rules and regulations for the construction, alteration, removal,
demolition, equipment, use and occupancy, location and maintenance of buildings
and structures, the approved editions of the following nationally recognized
codes, as adopted by the State of Idaho or the Idaho Building Code Board:
      1.   International Building Code, including all rules promulgated by the
Idaho Building Code Board to provide equivalency with the provisions of the
Americans With Disabilities Act Accessibility Guidelines and the Federal Fair
Housing Act Accessibility Guidelines.
      2.   International Residential Code, parts I through IV and IX.
      3.   International Energy Conservation Code.
      4.   International Fire Code.
   B.   Successive Versions Adopted: The adopted versions of the foregoing
codes shall be deemed superseded by successive versions of such codes as they
are adopted by the Idaho Building Code Board, effective on the date any such
codes are made effective by the Idaho Building Code Board. (Ord. 238; amd. 2018
Code)
   C.   Copies On File: One copy each of the adopted versions of the codes
adopted in subsection A of this section, either in hard copy or electronic
format, shall be duly certified and kept on file in the Office of the City
Clerk-Treasurer for use and examination by the public. (2018 Code)
7-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
   A.   Whenever the words "Municipality" or "City" are used in the Building
Code, they shall be held to mean the City of Winchester.
   B.   Whenever the term "Corporate Counsel" is used in the Building Code, it
shall be held to mean the attorney for the City of Winchester. (1990 Code §4-
402)
7-3-3: RIGHT OF ENTRY:
The building official or other officer appointed by the City Council to act as
the building official under the Building Code shall, in the discharge of his
official duties, and upon proper identification, have authority to enter any
building, structure or premises at any reasonable hour. (1990 Code §4-403)
7-3-4: BUILDING PERMIT FEES:
   A.   Payment Of Fees: The required fee for each building permit shall
accompany every application for a building permit, or the City Clerk-Treasurer
is authorized not to accept the same. Additional fees may be charged for
checking plans and specifications or for inspection services. (1990 Code §4-
404; amd. 2018 Code)
7-3-5: PENALTY:
Any person who violates any of the provisions of this chapter, or the codes
adopted in section 7-3-1 of this chapter, shall be deemed guilty of a
misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be subject to penalty as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (2018 Code)
CHAPTER 4
MOVING BUILDINGS
SECTION:
7-4-1: Permit Required; Fee
7-4-2: Bond Or Liability Insurance
7-4-1: PERMIT REQUIRED; FEE:
   A.   Permit Requirements: It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or
corporation to move any house, building or other structure of any kind or
nature upon, over, along or across any of the streets or alleys in the City
without first obtaining from the City Clerk-Treasurer a permit therefor, which
said permit shall state the following:
      1.   The name of the owner of said house, building or other structure.
      2.   The name of the person to whom the said permit is granted.
      3.   The place from which and the place to which it is desired to move
the said house, building or other structure.
      4.   The streets and alleys along, over, upon and across which it is
desired to move the same.
      5.   The length of time required to be fixed by the City Council. (1990
Code §4-301)
   B.   Permit Fee: The applicant for the permit provided for in subsection A
of this section shall pay to the Clerk-Treasurer the sum of five dollars
($5.00) for each and every permit so issued by him, which said money shall be
accounted for by the said Clerk-Treasurer in the same manner as are other
monies collected by other officials of the City. (1990 Code §4-304)
7-4-2: BOND OR LIABILITY INSURANCE:
   A.   Sufficient Bond Or Insurance Filed: Before the permit shall be granted
by the Clerk-Treasurer, the applicant for such permit shall file with the City
Clerk-Treasurer a good and sufficient bond or liability insurance policy in a
sum to be fixed by the City Clerk-Treasurer, saving the City harmless from any
accident or damages that may result from the moving of such house, building, or
other structure, which said bond shall be approved by the City Attorney. (1990
Code §4-302)
   B.   Filing Continuous Bond: If the person, firm or corporation making
application for the permit provided for in this chapter shall be regularly
engaged in the business of moving houses, buildings and other structures in the
City, the said person, firm or corporation may, upon application to the City
Clerk- Treasurer, be permitted to file a continuing bond or liability insurance
policy conditioned as provided in this chapter, which said bond or insurance
policy shall cover all moving of houses, buildings and other structures, in
which the said person, firm or corporation may be engaged during the fiscal
year in which said application is made, and thereafter it shall not be
necessary for said person, firm or corporation to file a separate bond or
liability insurance policy with each and every application for the permit
provided for in this chapter. (1990 Code §4-303)
CHAPTER 5
MOBILE/MANUFACTURED HOME PARKS
SECTION:
7-5-1: Purpose
7-5-2: Definitions
7-5-3: Permit Required; Application
7-5-4: Park Requirements And Restrictions
7-5-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to regulate the use of land for mobile home
parks and to establish standards for the development of such parks in order to
protect the health and safety of the community. (1990 Code §4-801)
7-5-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following words and phrases shall be
defined as follows.
MANUFACTURED HOME/MOBILE HOME PARK: A tract of land under unified ownership
developed for the purpose of providing nontransient rental space for parking
manufactured homes on individual spaces within its confines.
MOBILE/MANUFACTURED HOME:
   A.   Housing designed for long term residential use and built off site in a
factory setting, and then transported to a site for installation and use when
connected to required utilities.
   B.   Mobile/manufactured homes are divided into classes as specified in the
definition of "mobile/manufactured homes" in section
8-2-2 of this Code. (1990 Code §4-802)
7-5-3: PERMIT REQUIRED; APPLICATION:
   A.   A permit is required to operate or maintain a manufactured or mobile
home park.
   B.   Applications are available through City Hall. (1990 Code §4-803)
7-5-4: PARK REQUIREMENTS AND RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Minimum Park Area And Access: A mobile/manufactured home park shall
have a minimum of one acre, and shall include sufficient frontage on a public
street or road to allow safe ingress and egress.
   B.   Density And Minimum Lot Size: The maximum density for a mobile/
manufactured home park shall be eight (8) units per gross acre, and each
mobile/manufactured home park lot shall contain a minimum of five thousand
(5,000) square feet. The maximum lot coverage for each mobile/manufactured home
lot shall be sixty percent (60%). Interior park drives, public street rights-
of-way, and common areas used for parking or other park purposes are excluded
from the five thousand (5,000) square feet per unit area requirement.
   C.   Setbacks:
      1.   A minimum setback for a mobile/manufactured home shall be twenty
feet (20') from the property line adjacent to the front access road.
      2.   No mobile/manufactured home shall be located closer than three feet
(3') to the boundary line on either side of the mobile/manufactured home lot,
or closer than ten feet (10') to the front boundary of said lot, or closer than
five feet (5') to the rear boundary line of said lot, or closer than fifteen
feet (15') to any other mobile/manufactured home or permanent structure within
the mobile home park.
   D.   Lots Numbered: Each mobile/manufactured home lot shall be numbered. The
numbers shall be clearly visible from the park's interior drives/streets.
   E.   Interior Park Drives: Each mobile/manufactured home lot or space within
a mobile/manufactured home park shall have direct access to an interior park
drive and shall not have individual access to a public right-of-way. Interior
park drives shall consist of a minimum of twenty five feet (25') with at least
a gravel surface and there shall be no parking on either side of the drive.
Layout of mobile/manufactured home park's interior drives shall be in such a
manner as to provide adequate maneuvering for emergency vehicles. A mobile/
manufactured home park with only one interior drive may be required to provide
an emergency vehicle turnaround with a diameter of fifty two feet (52').
   F.   Utility Connections, Anchors, Pads: Each mobile/manufactured home lot
shall be provided with utility connections, ground anchors, piers or pads and
stabilizing connections of sufficient size to properly accommodate the mobile/
manufactured home unit in accordance with the manufacturer's specifications and
code requirement. All mobile/manufactured homes within the park shall be
skirted.
   G.   Landscaping: Landscaping in the mobile/manufactured home park shall be
provided in accordance with the following minimum requirements:
      1.   Peripheral Screening: The mobile/manufactured home park owner shall
provide peripheral site screening of trees, shrubs or other suitable sight
obstructing screen or fence.
      2.   Lawn Or Ground Cover: Lawn or other suitable ground cover shall be
provided for all open spaces other than access drives and parking circulation.
   H.   Confinement Of Runoff: Control of surface water runoff shall be
provided to confine all runoff to the property, or to drainage facilities
within public rights-of-way. (1990 Code §4-804)
   I.   Maintenance Agreement: A maintenance agreement, approved by the City
Council or its designee, shall be provided to assure the continued operation
and maintenance of interior drives, utilities, landscaping and solid waste
management. The park owner will be responsible for the provision of a suitable
guarantee that the park will be constructed within a two (2) year time period
and/or in accordance with standards set forth by the City Council. (1990 Code
§4-804; amd. 2018 Code)
   J.   Sewers: Each mobile/manufactured home lot shall be connected to a City
sewer system approved by the proper jurisdiction.
   K.   Storage Of Home Prohibited: No mobile/manufactured home shall be hauled
to, or stored within a mobile/manufactured home park unless it is properly
erected on a site approved for such use.
   L.   Animals: Aviaries, poultry, farm animals and horses are prohibited.
   M.   Alteration Or Enlargement Of Existing Parks: Mobile/manufactured home
parks in existence as of the effective date hereof shall be permitted to
continue as an established land use but shall not be altered so as to deviate
below the minimum standards of this chapter. Any addition to an existing
mobile/manufactured home park shall meet all of the standards required by this
chapter. If an addition or series of additions result in the doubling of the
size of an existing mobile/manufactured home park, then the entire park shall
be required to meet all standards required by this chapter. (1990 Code §4-804)
CHAPTER 6
RECREATIONAL VEHICLE PARKS
SECTION:
7-6-1: Purpose
7-6-2: Definitions
7-6-3: Permit Required; Application
7-6-4: Park Requirements And Restrictions
7-6-5: Parking And Storage Of Certain Vehicles
7-6-1: PURPOSE:
The City Council hereby finds and declares that the indiscriminate placement
and use of recreational vehicles (RVs) on individual lots within the City
threatens the health and safety of citizens, and damages property values. In
order to protect property values, to preserve the intent of the City
comprehensive plan, and to promote the general safety and welfare of the
citizens of the City, recreational vehicles shall be located only within
approved recreational vehicle parks, or as otherwise allowed in this Code 1 .
(Ord., 3-6-1995)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 8, chapter 5 of this Code.
7-6-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
RV PARK: A tract of land with one or more spaces rented for the parking of
recreational vehicles.
RECREATIONAL VEHICLE: A wheeled vehicle less than ten feet (10') in width at
its widest point, self-propelled or unpowered, and/or qualifying for a State of
Idaho recreational vehicle permit. (Ord., 3-6-1995)
7-6-3: PERMIT REQUIRED; APPLICATION:
   A.   Permit Required: A permit is required to operate or maintain any
recreational vehicle park. Applications for such permits shall be made to the
City Council through the City Clerk-Treasurer. The City Council shall then act
upon the application either granting or denying said application. (Ord., 3-6-
1995; amd. 2018 Code)
   B.   Transfer Of Permit:
      1.   No recreational vehicle park permit shall be transferrable. Every
person holding such a permit shall give notice in writing to the City within
five (5) days after having sold, transferred or otherwise disposed of any
interest in, or control of, an RV facility, unless a new permit has been
granted to subsequent owners or if an application for a new permit is pending.
      2.   Applications for permits by prospective new owners may be made in
advance of any sale or transfer, and shall be approved if the terms of the
applicable ordinances are met.
   C.   Plot Plan: A recreational vehicle park permit holder shall maintain a
current plot plan of each recreational vehicle park and ensure that such
current plot plan is on file with the City Clerk-Treasurer.
   D.   Permit Revocation Or Suspension: The City Council is hereby authorized
to revoke or suspend any recreational vehicle park permit issued hereunder if,
after due investigation, it determines that the holder thereof has violated any
of the provisions of this chapter or that any recreational vehicle park is
being maintained or operated in an unsanitary or unsafe manner, or, because of
the manner of operation, constitutes a public nuisance. (Ord., 3-6-1995)
7-6-4: PARK REQUIREMENTS AND RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Alteration Or Enlargement Of Existing Parks: Recreational vehicle parks
in use as of the effective date hereof shall be permitted to continue as an
established land use, but shall not be altered, in either construction or
operation, so as to cause any deviation from the minimum standards of this
chapter, insofar as the pre-existing use complies with this chapter on the
effective date hereof. If a nonconforming recreational vehicle park is enlarged
in either area or in usage (e.g., number of spaces available for rental or an
increase in seasonal availability of rental spaces), the entire park shall be
subject to the provisions hereof, specifically including, but not limited to,
the standards herein and the requirement of a permit.
   B.   Records Required: Every recreational vehicle park shall at all times
keep a register of all guests or tenants which shall be open to inspection by
State, Federal, and City officials. Said register shall contain the following
information:
      1.   Names and addresses of each guest or tenant.
      2.   Dates of entrance and departure.
      3.   Vehicle registration numbers and state of issue of each recreational
vehicle and tow vehicle.
   C.   Maintenance: Each recreational vehicle park shall be kept in a clean,
orderly and sanitary condition at all times.
   D.   Fire Protection: Each recreational vehicle park shall be subject to
inspection by the City Fire Chief and shall have installed and maintained fire
protection equipment such as fire extinguishers, fire hydrants and other
equipment in such quantities, qualities and locations as specified by said Fire
Chief, and as may be necessary to meet all applicable Building and Life Safety
Codes. Open fires shall not be allowed in a recreational vehicle park except in
locations and in facilities approved by the Fire Chief.
   E.   Interior Park Drives: All spaces within the recreational vehicle park
shall have direct access to an interior roadway not less than twenty five feet
(25') in width which shall have unobstructed access to a public street or
highway. Dead-end roadways shall provide adequate vehicle turning space, or a
cul-de-sac with not less than a fifty two foot (52') diameter exclusive of
parking.
   F.   Landscaping And Screening: The recreational vehicle park boundaries
shall be reasonably screened from outside view, whether by barriers of
ornamental fences, walls, trees or shrubs to assure reasonable integration with
adjoining land usages and to assure the health, safety and quiet enjoyment of
the area.
   G.   Occupant Improvement: Recreational vehicle park space occupants shall
not be permitted to erect or install any structures.
   H.   Utilities: All recreational vehicle spaces will be serviced by water,
sewer, and electrical hookups. Generators on individual recreational vehicles
will not be allowed to operate between the hours of seven o'clock (7:00) P.M.
and nine o'clock (9:00) A.M.
   I.   Storage Of Hazardous Materials: Storage of hazardous or potentially
hazardous materials shall not be allowed beneath recreational vehicles.
Hazardous or potentially hazardous materials include, but are not limited to,
flammable liquids, combustible liquids, compressed gas, combustible waste
matter, fireworks, firearms, or ammunition. (Ord., 3-6-1995)
7-6-5: PARKING AND STORAGE OF CERTAIN VEHICLES:
   A.   Automotive vehicles or trailer, or any kind or type of recreational
vehicle without current license plates shall not be parked or stored on any
residentially zoned property other than in completely enclosed buildings or
carports. However, one (1) boat and one (1) unoccupied travel trailer or other
recreational vehicle may be stored in the side or rear yard.
   B.   No trailer, camper or other recreational vehicle parked or stored
within the city limits shall be connected to water and/or sewer unless located
in an approved recreation vehicle park, except as specifically allowed herein.
   C.   Trailers, campers, or other recreational vehicle units shall not be
stored on city property or city rights-of-way, or in such a manner as to
infringe upon access to such property or right-of-way.
   D.   Trailers, campers, or other recreational vehicles shall not be occupied
as permanent or temporary dwellings except under the following conditions:
      1.   In an approved recreation vehicle park.
      2.   As a temporary building during construction and then only after the
issuance of a building permit for such construction.
      3.   As a temporary guest facility for no more than fourteen (14) days
during a thirty (30) day period.
      4.   A Homeowner may apply to the City Council, through the City Clerk to
use a trailer, camper, or other recreational vehicle as a temporary dwelling
for more than fourteen (14) days during a thirty (30) day period. Said
application must be made at the regular City Council meeting held prior to the
beginning the proposed use. The application must include duration of the use
requested, demonstrate appropriate use of appropriate water, sewage and
sanitation service, and that the immediate adjoining properties have no
objection to the proposed use request. The City Council, may at it's sole
discretion, grant or deny the application. (Ord. 210, 3-6-1995; amd. Ord. 293,
3-4-2021)
TITLE 8
ZONING REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
TITLE, AUTHORITY AND PURPOSES
SECTION:
8-1-1: Title And Authority
8-1-2: General Purposes
8-1-3: Minimum Requirements; Prevailing Provisions
8-1-4: Severability
8-1-1: TITLE AND AUTHORITY:
   A.   Title: This title shall be known as the ZONING ORDINANCE OF THE CITY OF
WINCHESTER, IDAHO. It shall consist of the following text in this title and a
"zoning map" which readily identifies the location of districts and
subdistricts.
   B.   Authority: This title is adopted pursuant to authority granted by Idaho
Code title 67, chapter 65 and article XII, section 2 of the Idaho Constitution,
as amended and codified. (Ord. 275, 4-2-2015)
8-1-2: GENERAL PURPOSES:
It is the intent of the City Council to provide uniform, equitable and
reasonable standards to govern the usage of land and structures. In order to
promote the health, safety and general welfare, the City seeks:
   A.   To ensure that adequate public facilities and services are provided to
persons at a reasonable cost.
   B.   To protect against fire, nuisances, and other hazards.
   C.   To conserve and stabilize property values.
   D.   To avoid air and water pollution.
   E.   To ensure that the development of land is commensurate with the
physical characteristics of the land.
   F.   To stabilize expectations regarding future development. (Ord. 275, 4-2-
2015)
8-1-3: MINIMUM REQUIREMENTS; PREVAILING PROVISIONS:
In their interpretation and application, the provisions of this title are held
to be minimum requirements. Whenever requirements of this title conflict with
the requirements of any other lawfully adopted rules, regulations, ordinances,
or resolutions, that imposing the higher standards shall govern. (Ord. 275, 4-
2-2015)
8-1-4: SEVERABILITY:
Should any section of this title be declared by the courts to be
unconstitutional or invalid, such decision shall not affect the validity of
this title as a whole or any other part. (Ord. 275, 4-2-2015)
CHAPTER 2
ZONING DEFINITIONS
SECTION:
8-2-1: Interpretation
8-2-2: Terms Defined
8-2-1: INTERPRETATION:
   A.   Words not defined herein shall be given the meanings ordinarily applied
to such words.
   B.   The present tense includes the future tense, the singular number
includes the plural, and the plural number includes the singular.
   C.   The word "shall" is a mandatory requirement; the word "may" is a
permissive requirement; and the word "should" is a preferred requirement. (Ord.
275, 4-2-2015)
8-2-2: TERMS DEFINED:
For the purpose of this title, the following terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
ACCESSORY USE OF BUILDING: A subordinate use of a building customarily incident
to and located upon the same lot occupied by the main building or utilized for
the main purpose.
ACREAGE: Any tract or parcel of land which has not been subdivided or platted.
AGRICULTURE: The tilling of the soil, the raising of crops, horticulture,
livestock, farming, dairying, or animal husbandry, including all uses,
customarily accessory and incidental thereto but not including slaughterhouses,
fertilizer works, bone yards or plants for the reduction of animal matter.
ALLEY: A street or way shown on the official plat of the City or its additions
and designated therein as an alley.
ALTER; ALTERATIONS: Any change, addition or modification in construction or
occupancy.
APARTMENT HOUSE: A building or portion thereof used or intended to be used as
the home of three (3) or more families or households living independently of
each other.
ASSISTED LIVING FACILITY: A facility or residence operated as either a profit
or nonprofit for the purpose of providing necessary supervision, personal
assistance, meals and lodging to adults not related to the owner.
AUTO WRECKING OR JUNK YARDS: Any place where two (2) or more motor vehicles not
in running condition, or parts thereof, are stored in the open and are not
being restored to operation; any land, building or structure used for wrecking
or storing of such motor vehicles or parts thereof and including any farm
